Geography Lecture: Why We Should Learn Foreign Geography (Part 2) 83

— Professor Huang Guozhang, Department of Geography, Central University

The above is a theoretical discussion. Now, let's take the geographical background of Japan's expansion overseas as an example to illustrate how important geographical knowledge in the late Ming Dynasty was for understanding international relations!

Japan is an island nation located only one day's sea journey from China. Although its area is less than 150,000 square miles, it has a population of 64 million, averaging over 400 people per square mile. The population per square mile of cultivated land is even higher, around 2,500. The density of the population can be imagined. Japan is not only densely populated, but also its population is increasing rapidly, with an annual increase of between 900,000 and 1 million. Since Japan is an island nation surrounded by the ocean on all sides, its land area cannot be expanded. Therefore, Japan's population problem has always been very serious.

There are three possible ways to solve Japan's population problem: strengthen the productive capacity of the country's land, engage in domestic and international migration, and seek large-scale development of the country's industry. Now, let's explain them one by one.

Expanding farmland – All plains and gently sloping hills have been reclaimed as farmland for growing grain. Experts estimate that Japan still has 4 to 5 million acres of arable land, half of which could be developed into rice paddies and could supply food for 20 million people. In other words, it could accommodate Japan's population increase within the next 20 years. However, according to statistics from 1905 to 1925, Japan averaged less than 100,000 acres of reclaimed land per year. It is undoubtedly impossible to develop all 4 to 5 million acres of wasteland into fertile land within 20 years.

Increasing the yield per acre of farmland – The yield of Japanese crops per unit of cultivated land does show an increase, but it is far less rapid than the population increase. Moreover, the productivity of land has a certain limit and cannot increase indefinitely like the population.

Domestic migration – 1. Migration to Hokkaido: The population distribution on the main islands of Japan is not very even, and there are still many sparsely populated areas. The population density of Hokkaido is only one-fifth of the average population density of the country. Therefore, the Japanese government has planned to encourage migration to Hokkaido. However, the climate in Hokkaido is very cold and unsuitable for people from central and southern Japan to live there. As a result, this plan failed. 2. Migration to places like Korea, Taiwan, and Sakhalin Island: Japan has seized a lot of land from our country, accounting for 60% of the area of the main islands of Japan, and Korea and Taiwan are the main parts of it. These places are better than Hokkaido, with climates similar to those of central and southern Japan, and similar products. It should be easy to move the surplus Japanese population to these places, but the population of these places is already very dense, with more than 210 people per square mile, and Taiwan has even more than 360 people. Moreover, the living standards of the people in these places are lower than those of the Japanese, making it difficult for the Japanese to compete with them in terms of living. In addition, the population growth rate in these places is higher than that in Japan. According to statistics from 1925, the increase rate per thousand people in Japan was 13.4, in Korea it was 26.1, and in Taiwan it was 18.6. Because of these various factors, these places cannot accommodate many Japanese immigrants each year. Since Korea became affiliated with Japan, the average number of Japanese immigrants each year has been less than 15,000. After 1915, the average number of Japanese immigrants to Taiwan has been even less than 5,000. Compared with Japan's annual increase of 900,000 to 1 million people, it is really not helpful. In addition, Japan seized the southern part of Sakhalin Island from the Russians, which is even colder than Hokkaido, and the Japanese are even more reluctant to go there. After the European War, Japan gained the right to manage several islands in the Pacific Ocean that formerly belonged to Germany because of its contribution to the war. However, although these small islands have military value, they are not enough to accommodate a large number of Japanese immigrants. Since the takeover, only about 30,000 Japanese have resided on those islands.

Overseas migration – In 1931, the total number of Japanese overseas residents was no more than 750,000, which is less than the number of people Japan increases in one year. Moreover, these overseas residents also include many Koreans and Taiwanese, as well as Japanese students studying abroad, diplomats, and naval and army personnel. The formal number of overseas residents is only about 700,000. Compared with the 630,000 overseas residents in 1926, the increase was only 120,000 in five years, with an average of only 24,000 people per year. Among these immigrants, 70% were engaged in reclamation in the Amazon River basin in South America, which is sparsely populated, due to the Japanese government's various rewards and the Brazilian government's preferential treatment. But everyone knows how unsuitable the Amazon River basin is for habitation, as it is a hot and humid forest area. It is within our expectation that Japanese immigrants cannot develop greatly here. In North American countries, the Japanese could have competed with white people by taking advantage of their lower living standards, but the Japanese are not only unwelcome in these countries, but also the restrictions on immigration mean that this path is impassable. In the Philippines, the South Seas Islands, and the Northeast region of our country, the Japanese feel that the competition from the Chinese and other local people is too fierce, and they cannot live there for long. From this, it can be seen that although domestic and overseas migration can help with Japan's population problem, this assistance is ultimately limited, and other plans must be made.

(5) Developing industry – Developing industry can directly increase national wealth and indirectly use this wealth to buy various living materials from abroad, accommodating the increased population. Industrial development has relatively no end and is the best way to solve the population problem. Therefore, since the Meiji Restoration, Japan has followed in the footsteps of Britain and actively engaged in industrial development. Now, it has achieved great results. The development of the cotton weaving industry is second only to that of Britain and the United States, and the prosperity of the silk manufacturing industry is the highest in the world. Other industries, such as the steel industry, shipbuilding industry, and paper industry, all occupy a considerable position internationally. The number of domestic workers has increased by an average of 47,000 people per year from 1894 to 1926. The degree of national industrialization has become more and more significant. Today, Japan has indeed become an important industrial country in the world.

There are many reasons why Japanese industry has been able to develop, but the Sino-Japanese War, the Russo-Japanese War, and the three major battles of the European War are the biggest keys: As a result of the Sino-Japanese War in 1894-1895, all unequal treaties were cancelled, and Japan's national prestige was enhanced. All kinds of undertakings have since risen, and the manufacturing industry has also risen under various conditions such as the acquisition of Korea and Taiwan, the expansion of the market for goods and raw materials, and the government's implementation of protectionist tariff policies. As a result of the Russo-Japanese War in 1904-1905, Japan jumped to become a first-class power and obtained economic interests in South Manchuria. Its national strength became even stronger, and its industry also developed rapidly. In the European War of 1914-1918, Japan took advantage of the troubles in the West, which had no time to look eastward, and expanded the Eastern market as much as possible. Industry showed even more rapid progress. During the war, the number of workers increased by an average of 160,000 to 170,000 per year, and it eventually became one of the world's major industrial countries. This can be said to be a heaven-sent opportunity for the development of Japanese industry. In addition to the victory in foreign wars, other factors such as the development of overseas shipping, low labor costs, and the rise of hydropower projects have all promoted the development of Japanese industry.

Although Japanese industry has developed rapidly, there are many crises lurking ahead, and it is really not optimistic. Although there is no shortage of workers and labor costs are very low, technical skills are inferior compared to Europe and the United States. Moreover, the country's wealth is not very large. The average annual income per person is not only lower than that of the four countries of the United States, Britain, France, and Germany, but is simply less than half of that of Italy, so domestic purchasing power is very weak. But these are not the biggest dangers. The lack of raw materials and the lack of energy sources are the biggest blows to the development of Japanese industry. The reserves of iron ore are not large, and the annual output is not enough to supply even one-tenth of its own needs. The rest must be supplied from Korea, China, and the Malay Peninsula. The cotton required by the cotton spinning industry comes almost entirely from the United States, India, China, and other places. There is very little domestic production, and cotton imports always account for the largest share of Japanese imports. Wool is also rarely produced domestically because pastures have been converted into farms and there are very few sheep. Coal and copper are two of Japan's most important mineral products. Although there are large reserves of coal, the quality of the coal is poor, and very little can be used for coking. The import volume of copper is also greater than the export volume. The reserves of oil are also very scarce, and the production volume is one-tenth of the consumption volume. Only a portion of hydropower can be used for industry, and when the river flow is at its lowest, the total hydropower volume is only 6 million horsepower, which is not enough to make up for this shortcoming.

One reason why Japan promoted the realization of the puppet state of Manchukuo and is so eager to expand its influence in the provinces of North China is that North China and Northeast China are both coal and iron producing regions of China. The abundance of geographical advantages and the convenience of transportation are no less than the Rhine River basin in Europe. It is the center of heavy industry in the Far East in the future. By obtaining Northeast China and North China, Japan can not only make up for its lack of coal and iron and develop heavy industry on a large scale, but also make the whole of China a permanent sales market for Japanese heavy industrial products, and the surplus products can be sold to all parts of the world at low prices. If China loses Northeast China and North China, the development of domestic heavy industry will be declared hopeless, because other than these two regions, it can be said that there is no second coal and iron producing region in China, and it is impossible to find a second coal and iron producing region that is so abundant in both coal and iron.

Japan's expansion of influence in North China is not only due to the need for coal and iron, but also for the supply of cotton raw materials and for finding a market for the surplus grain in Northeast China. Originally, the agricultural products of the provinces in Northeast China were mainly soybeans, wheat, sorghum, and corn. Soybeans have a world market, while wheat, sorghum, and corn not only do not have an international market, but are also not needed by the densely populated areas of Japan. What Japan needs is rice and cotton, and cotton is the foundation of Japanese industry and is not produced within Japan, so the need is even more urgent. The growing season in the three northeastern provinces is too short, and most areas cannot grow cotton, which cannot supply all of its needs. The crops in North China are the same as those in Northeast China, and it is also a major cotton producing area. If a large amount of cotton is planted in North China, it can not only supply the needs of its own textile industry, but also the grain needed in North China can be supplied by Northeast China. The cotton can be transported to Osaka, processed, and then transported back to North China and Northeast China to supply the people's need for clothing. It can really be called a win-win situation. In addition, another reason for Japan's expansion of influence in Northeast China and North China is to prevent the southward expansion of Soviet Russian influence. This point will not be discussed for the time being due to time constraints.

Page 9

Record of a Journey Through the Desert Regions (12) 84

— Jin Dui

15. Customs of the Mongol and Hui People in Ningxia

In Ningxia, Mongol and Hui people live together, and the etiquette and customs of their society are deeply rooted in religion. Compared to Han customs, they are vastly different. Here, I will record the unique customs of weddings, funerals, and seasonal observances to provide reference for scholars studying folklore.

Mongol Customs: Courage and a fondness for fighting are hereditary traits of the Mongolian people. Farming is naturally unsuitable for them. However, Mongolians possess strong physiques, making nomadic life, roaming freely in the vast deserts, perfectly suited to their nature. They spend their days wandering in the embrace of nature, herding sheep, tending camels, and managing horses. Living under the open sky and sleeping on the ground, they feed on mutton and reside in tents, moving with the availability of water and grass. This lifestyle necessitates a strong physique, so they rarely fall ill and are almost ashamed to be sick. They lack medicine and medical care, relying instead on heating stones to cauterize themselves, allowing nature to heal them. Their sole faith lies in the Buddha statues and Lama monks enshrined in temples. The following describes Mongolian weddings, funerals, and their annual reverence for Buddhist lamas. (A) Weddings and Funerals: They first meet in private, without parental involvement or matchmakers. Love is extremely free, with horse racing and betting determining the outcome. Dowries are lavish, with cattle, sheep, and wealth held separately by each spouse. Marital discord requires minimal formalities for divorce. Funerals involve sky burials or cremations. After the death of parents, sons and daughters gather to weep and express their grief fully. They consult a Lama to determine the burial site. For sky burials, the corpse is left in the mountains or desert, and they observe the area the next day. If the corpse is completely consumed by birds and beasts, it is considered a good omen; otherwise, they mourn and move the body to another location, asking the Lama to chant scriptures and pray until the corpse is consumed by beasts, thus averting misfortune. For cremations, the corpse is taken to a mountain slope with a pit, a stove entrance is opened beside it, and the corpse is placed inside to be burned. Sons and daughters loosen their braids and wear their clothes inside out for a month, without visiting the grave or holding memorial services. On anniversary dates, they invite Lamas to chant scriptures and pray. (B) Seasonal Observances: On "New Year's Day," they go to the temple to kowtow to the Lama, return to their yurts for tea, and then return to the temple to circle it more than ten times. The sick lie prostrate on the ground, circling once or twice. They do not give New Year's greetings or invite relatives and friends for tea, and they avoid lending fire to others. On the fifteenth day, they all go to the Great Lama to be blessed by a touch on the head. The Lama uses a wooden pole with red cloth tied to it to strike people randomly. Those who are struck appear delighted, while those who have not been struck wait patiently, often for four or five days. On June 15th, they again go to the Great Lama for blessings and strikes. In all the temples, from the first to the fifteenth day of the first and sixth lunar months, Lamas chant scriptures. The Great Lama sits high on a platform, chanting scriptures, while thirty-two people in colorful robes and python robes of various colors, representing celestial kings, bodhisattvas, ox-headed demons, horse-faced guardians, and other figures, dance on the temple platform. First, trumpets and horns are blown, and drums and music are played, welcoming them in pairs from within. They dance on the altar and use fried noodles and butter to knead a naked human figure, placing it on a triangular wooden plate lined with triangular silk. One of the celestial kings uses a small wooden sword to dismember it. After the chanting is finished, they are sent off with drums and gongs, far beyond the temple, one or two miles away, before returning. On this day, temple officials collect donations from Han and Mongolian people. At the New Year, they take river ice and stack it against the walls, connecting piece by piece. On "New Year's Eve," they burn incense and chant scriptures in their rooms. Those who have lost their parents kowtow and weep before the whole family sits together for tea and then sleeps.

Hui Customs: Hui people are diligent and clean, abstaining from tobacco, alcohol, and other vices. They possess a martial spirit and adhere to Islam, i.e., the "Islamic" religion. The translated meaning of "Islam" is peace. Islam regards the "Quran" as its most precious scripture, which can be considered the constitution of Islam and the basis of faith for Muslims. The following is a summary of the unique aspects of the marriage, funeral, and seasonal customs of the Hui people in Ningxia. (A) Weddings and Funerals: Marriage is not selective based on wealth, only choosing good and virtuous families. Matchmakers convey proposals and inquire about family backgrounds, establishing kinship and using engagement gifts to confirm the arrangement. Religious leaders are invited to write the marriage contract, and a day or two before the wedding, the bride's family prepares the dowry, sending messengers to decorate the groom's house. The amount of the dowry usually follows religious guidelines, with the daughter receiving half of what a son would inherit. On the wedding day, the bride is presented to the groom's parents, and the groom presents gifts to the bride's family. When parents are critically ill, there is silence inside and outside the house. The sick person is placed in the main room, and the children constantly recite the Quran. According to Muslims, this is to remind the sick person to focus on the faith and not be attached to the world. During the critical moment of passing away, the departure of the soul, no negligence is allowed. Once the person has passed away and is at peace, a mourning altar is set up, and funeral directors are hired. Clothing is changed in the room, and guests are not entertained for three days, nor is food prepared. Relatives and friends send food. Relatives, neighbors, and friends offer condolences and gifts. The burial clothes consist of three pieces for men and four pieces for women, all made of fine white cloth, regardless of wealth or status. A coffin is prepared, and the grave is dug without regard to feng shui or auspicious timing, with the burial taking place within three days. On the morning of the burial day, the deceased's body is washed, dressed, and placed in the coffin, which is then taken to the mosque. Religious leaders and guests perform funeral rites. At the grave, the filial son inspects the grave and prays before sealing the burial. After the burial, memorial services are held on the 7th, 40th, 100th day, the anniversary, the third anniversary, and the anniversary of the birth and death, with visiting the grave, chanting scriptures, giving alms, and scattering grain as the essential ways of filial piety. (B) Seasonal Observances: Islam calculates a year based on the sun's journey around the sky in 365 and a quarter days and nights. A year is calculated based on the moon's journey in twelve months, which is 354 and a third days and nights. The solar year is used for determining seasonal events, while the lunar year is used for recording human affairs. Therefore, all ceremonies are calculated based on a twelve-month cycle. Islam firmly believes in creation, with a single true God in heaven and earth who is not physical nor empty. He is supremely intelligent, infinitely subtle, without beginning or end, the great source of human nature and life, and the origin of all existence. The main tenets of faith include belief in God, belief in prophets, and belief in scriptures. There are five duties to worship God: "Remembrance," to never forget the true God; "Prayer," to pray five times a day, always purifying oneself before each prayer; "Fasting," to fast for a month each year, rotating every three years; "Alms," to give alms to the poor and needy each year; and "Pilgrimage," to make a pilgrimage to the holy land of Islam.

Kang Wang Assumes Office in Suiyuan as Commander-in-Chief of the Ih Meng League 85

Simultaneously Takes Office as Commander for Bandit Suppression in Dalah Banner

Over Five Hundred Han and Mongolian Attendees

Rong Xiang Exhorts Princes and Dukes to Serve the Country

Communication from Guisui: Zhasak Kangda Dorji of Dalah Banner recently held a swearing-in ceremony at the Suiyuan Hotel for his dual appointment as Commander-in-Chief of the Seven Banner Allied Forces of Ih Meng League and Commander for Bandit Suppression in Dalah Banner. Over five hundred Han and Mongolian dignitaries attended. Chairman Fu Zuoyi of Suiyuan Province represented the central government in administering the oath. Shakdurjab, the head of the Ih Meng League, also attended to deliver instructions. Princes Wang, Shi, E, and all the princes and dukes from various banners in Suiyuan attended the ceremony and delivered speeches, making it an unprecedented event in the border region. Among the speeches by the princes and dukes, the one by Rong Xiang, the chief administrator of Tumet Banner, was considered the most valuable. Rong Xiang possessed profound knowledge of Chinese classics and excelled in parallel prose, earning him the reputation of "Literary Giant of the Border Region." In his speech, from the perspective of a Mongolian and with the attitude of a scholar, he elaborated in detail on the historical contributions of the Mongolian people to the establishment of the nation and the preferential treatment the nation had given to the Mongolian people. The full text of his speech has been compiled and is excerpted below:

"Today is the day when Zhasak Kang of Dalah Banner is commissioned to hold the swearing-in ceremony for Commander-in-Chief of the Seven Banner Allied Forces of Ih Meng League and Commander for Bandit Suppression in Dalah Banner. I am deeply honored to be invited to attend this grand ceremony. As a Mongolian and a scholar, I would like to offer some humble contributions to Commander Kang and the princes, dukes, and chief administrators, based on the perspective of a Mongolian, the attitude of a scholar, and my thoughts today. I often hear our Mongolians from various leagues and banners mention that we are descendants of Genghis Khan, the Great Yuan Taizu, as a way to promote the achievements of our ancestors and prove the glory of our race. Historical records show that Genghis Khan was a great hero who shook ancient and modern times and conquered Europe and Asia. Not only do the Chinese know this, but people as far away as Europe and America are also familiar with him and admire him. Furthermore, according to the biographies of Mongolian princes and dukes, all hereditary princes and dukes of the various leagues and banners in Inner and Outer Mongolia are either descendants of Genghis Khan or descendants of his meritorious officials. Therefore, the princes, dukes, and all Mongolians of today are pleased to mention the achievements of Genghis Khan, considering it a glory of their race. This can be considered a well-founded claim, not simply using the power of a tiger to intimidate the masses. However, there is a point that we Mongolians should reflect on and that I must announce to you. No matter how great the character of our ancestors, no matter how vast their achievements, if the descendants themselves have no achievements to show to the world, then the glory and greatness of the ancestors still belong to the founding ancestors. For the descendants themselves, apart from serving as material for boasting, it is ultimately empty and useless, as the saying goes, 'It cannot fill your stomach.' Therefore, all of us who are descendants of the Great Khan should not forget the glorious deeds of our ancestors. At the same time, we must each strive to make some great and glorious contributions to the country, the region, the society, and the nation, so as not to be unworthy of being sacred sons and divine grandsons. In addition to highlighting the achievements of our ancestors, we will also have indelible achievements of our own. Furthermore, considering the historical positions of the princes and dukes, we need not discuss the Yuan and Ming dynasties. Even in the previous Qing dynasty, the princes and dukes of all our leagues and banners were granted titles and ranks that were hereditary. Was this achieved without reason? It was because, at the beginning of the Qing dynasty's entry into the Central Plains, the ancestors of our leagues and banners helped the Qing court to quell the bandits and pacify the regions, either by providing troops, donating horses, or personally leading troops into battle to help the Qing dynasty lay its foundation. Therefore, the current status of the princes and dukes was earned through the hard work and meritorious service of the ancestors of each banner. Regarding the countless contributions and efforts of the leagues during the Qing dynasty, it is impossible to recount them all. Taking my own banner, Tumet, as an example, when Prince Yu of the Qing dynasty, Dodo, used cavalry to attack the bandit Zhang Xianzhong, our banner donated thousands of horses, which led to the suppression of the bandits. During Emperor Kangxi's campaign against Galdan in the thirty-fifth year of his reign, the Uyi League, the Tumet Banner, and others sent cavalry to participate in the campaign, ultimately pacifying the great threat and ensuring peace on the border. Therefore, on the day of his return, Emperor Kangxi heavily renovated the temples in the banner territory and left behind armor, bows, arrows, swords, spears, saddles, and bridles as mementos. After the mid-Qing dynasty, when the Taiping Rebellion broke out, troops were often conscripted from our banner to assist in the battles. In total, seven thousand strong men were sent in three separate instances. After the rebellion was quelled, only about a thousand soldiers returned. Such was the case for our banner, and other banners had similar experiences. As for the eastern leagues, such as the Zhe Meng League and its subordinate banners, their sacrifices and losses were undoubtedly greater than those of our western leagues. From these past events, we can see that although the Qing dynasty treated our leagues and banners generously, the Mongolians repaid them in kind. In summary, based on the principle of reciprocity, the princes and dukes of our banners can be said to have earned the titles and honors bestowed upon them by the previous Qing dynasty. Since the establishment of the Republic of China more than twenty years ago, the nation's preferential treatment of the princes and dukes of the Mongolian banners has only increased. Not only were regulations created, but they were also put into practice. Princes of the second rank were promoted to princes of the first rank, and princes of the first rank were given double salaries. All other dukes, beile, beizi, and zhenfu were promoted according to the regulations. Since the establishment of the National Government, the central government's treatment of the princes and dukes of the Mongolian banners has been even more preferential. To ensure their self-preservation, security commissioners were established for them. To ensure their self-governance, local political committees were established for them. The nation spends countless public funds each year, only to ensure the survival of the Mongolians. The nation treats us Mongolians even better than the previous Qing dynasty. When we Mongolians search our hearts, can we say that our contributions to the nation are superior to our contributions to the previous Qing dynasty? Therefore, today, the princes and dukes of our banners, realizing the great kindness of the nation, should each strive to take on some responsibilities for the nation, so as not to simply accept the nation's grace without knowing how to repay it. I am also well aware that in the past twenty years, the leagues and banners did not lack the desire to repay the nation, but there were few opportunities. Although they wanted to contribute some effort, they did not know how. Fortunately, in recent months, Prince Pan and Prince Kang have taken on important roles in bandit suppression. This is an opportunity for the princes and dukes of our leagues and banners to strive to serve the country. If Prince Kang and the princes can understand the central government's sincere intention to support them and Chairman Fu's efforts to guide and promote them, and if they can strive together from the day they take office to achieve harmony and cooperation, so that both the Han and Mongolian people in the region can enjoy a peaceful and prosperous life, then devoting their efforts to their homeland is precisely the way to repay the nation. I am honored to participate in this grand ceremony and offer my humble opinions to the princes and dukes. May you consider them."

Ministry of Finance Recovers Salt Tax in Guizhou 86

Annual Subsidies from Sichuan Salt Transport Administration for Military Expenses

Salt Merchant System in Guizhou Province to Be Abolished Immediately

Communication from Guiyang: The supply of edible salt in Guizhou Province has historically been rotated from Sichuan Province. The salt distribution system has sometimes adopted a merchant recognition (认商) and coastal recognition (认岸) system, and other times adopted a free trading system. However, the merchant recognition system has been especially harmful to the people. During the era of Mao Wang's rule, the merchant recognition system was mostly adopted, allowing merchants to manipulate the market and causing the price of salt to rise from one or two dimes per catty to as much as six dimes per catty, causing great suffering to the people. Last summer, the new provincial government was established, and Li Zhonggong, the director of the Finance Department, conducted extensive research on the selection of these two systems. In the end, he resolutely implemented the free trading system. However, reform takes time, and the regulations were complicated, so he did not succeed during his term. After Wang Zhengying took over as the director of the Finance Department, he planned to completely resolve the salt affairs issue. He repeatedly consulted with the Sichuan Salt Transport Administration to seek to restore the system of subsidies for military expenses. Before the subsidies and the new salt law were finalized, he extended the merchant recognition period for one year, from September 1, 1935, to the end of August 1936. Now that the subsidies have been finalized and the central government has recovered the salt administration, the free trading system can be implemented early. The circumstances of this process are briefly described below:

Subsidies for Military Expenses

After the central government recovers the salt tax in Guizhou Province, the Sichuan Salt Transport Administration will directly allocate 1.5 million yuan to Guizhou Province for military expenses each year, as well as another 120,000 yuan for educational expenses, totaling 1.61 million yuan. All taxes, surcharges, and expenses related to Sichuan salt in Guizhou Province will be suspended from February 1, 1936. The Salt Affairs Supervision Bureau and the inspection stations that specifically collect surcharges on Sichuan salt will also be abolished.

Agreement Contents

The full text of the agreement between the Guizhou Provincial Government and the Sichuan Salt Transport Administration on subsidy measures is as follows: The Central Ministry of Finance will designate 1.5 million yuan to be allocated to the Guizhou Provincial Treasury annually from the Sichuan salt tax revenue, to be allocated monthly by the Sichuan Salt Transport Administration. From the date of this agreement, salt merchant recognition in Guizhou Province will be immediately abolished, and merchants will be allowed to trade freely in accordance with the regulations. No one is allowed to manipulate or monopolize the market. From the date of implementation of this agreement, the surcharges on Sichuan salt in Guizhou Province and all miscellaneous taxes will be immediately abolished, and no institution or organization in the two provinces may collect fees under any name. From the date of implementation of this agreement, all salt affairs agencies under the jurisdiction of Guizhou Province will be abolished, and the Sichuan Salt Transport Administration will restore the Guiyang Supervision and Anti-Smuggling Bureau and the Tongren, Dushan, and Panxian Anti-Smuggling Sub-Bureaus. The Guizhou Provincial Government is responsible for maintaining the integrity of the Sichuan salt in Guizhou and assisting in anti-smuggling efforts. Because the educational expenses in Guizhou Province are not covered due to the abolition of the surcharges on Sichuan salt, it is proposed to submit another case to the Ministry of Finance for review and approval, with an additional 10,000 yuan to be allocated monthly from the Sichuan salt tax. This agreement will be implemented from February 1, 1936, on a trial basis for one year.

Salt Affairs Office Abolished

Since the salt tax in Guizhou Province has been recovered by the central government and merchant recognition has been abolished, the Salt Affairs Office of the Finance Department and all salt tax collection agencies will be abolished from February 1st, according to a resolution passed by the standing committee of the provincial government, and will be closed by the end of February. Recently, the Salt Affairs Office of the Finance Department has been actively working to finalize various closing matters. The suspension of salt affairs expenses and surcharges has also been officially announced from February 1st. At the same time, the salt merchants of Renqi Yongsanan (仁綦永三岸) recently sent representatives Wu Luqin, Yang Fuxing, Liu Yaoxian, Ning Jisheng, etc., to the provincial government to present a petition, detailing the difficulties faced by the merchants in managing edible salt due to the establishment of the subsidies and the interruption of merchant recognition, and requesting the provincial government to find ways to provide relief. After receiving the petition, the provincial government submitted it to the 208th resolution meeting, handing it over to Mou Lin, Ye Yuanlong, and Wang Zhengying for review and approval.

Four Counties in Shandong Province Again Request That the Yellow River Be Allowed to Change Its Course 87

Cutting Bends and Straightening the Riverbed for Perpetual Peace and Security

Shandong Provincial Government Forwards Letter to the Yellow River Commission for Review

Communication from Jinan: Since the Yellow River breached the people's embankment in Juancheng County and flowed east, returning to the correct course through the Huanghuasi Koumen along the former Yellow River channel for fourteen years, the shape of the Yellow River's outlet has changed, coinciding with the advocacy of Li Yiqi, the former Chairman of the Yellow River Conservancy Commission. The people along the northern bank of the Yellow River embankment in Puyang, Fanxian, Shouyang, and other counties have suffered heavy losses because the Yellow River has breached its banks and flooded into the Golden Embankment through Taochengbu. Now that the Yellow River flows east from Juancheng County and enters the river through Huanghuasi, it has naturally cut bends and straightened its course, making it the most suitable path. In the future, not only will the Golden Embankment be perpetually safe and secure, but also the dangerous engineering projects on the southern bank, such as Liuzhuang and Zhukou on the official embankment, and Lishengtun, Kangtun, and Lilou on the people's embankment, as well as Liuyuan and Liaoqiao on the northern people's embankment, can all be avoided. Therefore, they jointly implore the provincial government not to block the Juancheng people's embankment again, but to allow the Yellow River to change its course through Huanghuasi. Currently, Liu Yude and others, representatives of the people of these counties, have sent another telegram to Chairman Chiang Kai-shek and the provincial government, reiterating their previous intention and criticizing the Yellow River Conservancy Commission's damming project by Kong Xiangrong, which has already failed. The old river is silted up, and it is already difficult to return to the old course. Even if it is forcibly closed, the breach this year will be either south or north, and the damming will be endless. They request that the Dongzhuang damming project be moved to repair the official embankment, so that the disaster areas of western Shandong and northern Jiangsu can be restored as soon as possible, and that the water be allowed to change its course. After receiving the telegram, the provincial government forwarded it to the Yellow River Conservancy Commission for review. The text of the telegram from the representatives of the people of the four counties is recorded below: "(Summary) The previous telegram and the report on the new breach of the Yancheng people's embankment taking a straight course should be understood. The reason for the urgent telegram is that according to Chairman Li's plan, Liuzhuang and Zhukou on the southern official embankment, and Lishengtun, Kangtun, and Lilou on the people's embankment, as well as Liuyuan and Liaoqiao on the northern people's embankment, will all be avoided, and there will be perpetual peace and security. If the Dongzhuang damming project is carried out, the breach this year will be either north or south, and the damming will be endless. Because the Dongzhuang damming project digs a diversion canal against the water flow, the small diversion canal has already been silted up, and the large diversion canal is even more ineffective, merely wasting labor and money. Moreover, the damming work is not even one-tenth completed. At this time, the work can be used to build the Taoshui Dam and move the damming to the official embankment. Moreover, the people of Juancheng along the old river, and the people south of the official embankment, as well as the people of Heze, Yuncheng, Juye, Dingtao, and Cao counties, all wish to move the damming. The Shandong Minguo Daily on February 14th reported that the water outflow from Huanghuasi was smooth, which can also be verified. And Qin, the county magistrate of Juancheng, previously dug the sixth gate of the official embankment to protect the Juancheng embankment, and now, taking advantage of the north wind, he is blocking the Juancheng gate, digging and blocking at will, which is clear upon investigation. Now that the old river is high and will soon stop flowing, the people of Hebei are boiling with resentment, and there is much public discussion. In addition to sending a telegram to Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, we hereby submit a telegram. Liu Yude, representative of Puyang, Fanxian, Shouyang, and other counties, bows."

Kunshan 88

Verdict on Murder Case Resulting from Pulling Rice Roots

Shi Daming, a farmer from Xiaolianjing, Pengjianzhen in Kunshan County, instructed his wife, Zhang, to go to the fields to pull out rice roots during the busy season of treating rice stem borers in November of this year. It is said that a disagreement led to an argument, and Shi Daming beat his wife with a tree root, unexpectedly causing her sudden death. The local public security bureau arrested and detained Shi Daming in the county, and after several court hearings, the verdict was announced the other day, sentencing Shi Daming to six months of imprisonment as a warning.

Wuxi 89

Skyrocketing Exchange Rate: Joint Discussion of Relief Measures

The Wuxi Carriage Industry, Tobacco Exchange, Liquor and Sauce Shop, Meat Industry, and Native Tobacco Trade Associations, due to the recent skyrocketing exchange rate in the city, where each yuan can be exchanged for 3,170 copper coins, invited leaders from over ten trade associations, including the Sauce and Liquor, Southern Goods, Grain, and Noodle Restaurants, to jointly discuss relief measures on the 23rd. They decided to send a letter to the county chamber of commerce, requesting the bank to accept exchanges, and stipulated that the market price of copper coins should be 3,000. The money markets in neighboring counties such as Suzhou, Changzhou, and Yixing are all lower than in Wuxi, averaging from 3,000 to 3,050. Shi Qinglin, the standing committee member of the Wuxi Tobacco Exchange Trade Association, went to Yixing to investigate the money market in order to understand the money market in the neighboring counties. He found that the money market in Yixing was 3,000, not as high as in Wuxi.

Dramatic Increase in the Number of Opium Addicts

Since the county launched the opium addicts' self-renewal registration, the number of opium addicts in each district has increased by more than 4,700. The existing opium dens are thriving, with opium smokers crowding in, making it difficult to cope. The county government has ordered each district chief to increase the number of opium dens as appropriate based on the actual situation in the area. After receiving the order, Qian Zhongliang, the first district chief, sent personnel to investigate. In addition to the existing dens, it is planned to add four more in Ximen Zhijie, Beitan, Malu, and Chong'an Temple. Yesterday, he reported back to the county government for verification.

Impersonating an Inspector Arrested

A middle-aged man came to the Wan'an Inn on Dongdajie in the city on the evening of the other day, wearing a black woolen cotton robe, a felt hat, leather shoes, a Vienna scarf around his neck, glasses, a badge on his chest, a fountain pen, and carrying a flashlight. He claimed to be an inspector from the Public Security Bureau and came to inspect the rooms. The inn believed him and handed over the guest registration book to the man. He first checked room number one and then number six. The innkeeper, Chen Jiadong, saw that he was not wearing a uniform and became suspicious. He asked to see his official documents but was unable to obtain them. He only took out a photo of the foreign comedic star "Laurel and Hardy," and realized that he was an impersonator. He immediately detained him and handed him over to the first branch of the Public Security Bureau for strict interrogation. According to his confession, his name is Guo Zhendong, from Anhui. Two round badges were found on his person, one reading "Strive to Save the Country" and the other reading "Central First Army Soldiers' Association Membership Badge," with the character "Constitution" in the middle. Two photos were found, one of Laurel and Hardy and one of Xu Lai. Eight business cards were also presented. Yesterday, he was transferred to the court for trial. It is reported that Guo's other name is Zhensheng, and he had previously impersonated a military officer in Danyang with Zhu Rongfu, defrauding people, and was detained by the Danyang County Government. He was released from prison on February 13th of this year.

Jiangyin 90

Dredging of Yingtian River in Progress

The dredging of the Yingtian River in the county has been underway for nearly a month since work began. The progress of the project is still considered rapid. The water draining project has been completed, and preparations are now being made to go down to the pond. The engineering office also convened a meeting of township and village chiefs and supervisors in the section the other day to discuss the project, resolving to levy three laborers per mu.

Song Renjie Arrested and Sent to the Province

Song Renjie, a native of the county, has a good reputation in the local area. He served as a supervisor in the Public Security Bureau a few years ago. Recently, someone reported to the Military and Political Department that he was involved in drug trafficking. The military department, based on the report, consulted the province on the 24th, ordering the county to arrest Song and detain him in the Public Security Bureau overnight before sending him to the province to be transferred to Beijing for interrogation. Chen Wenqi and Yao Yuxian, two other individuals involved, were also arrested outside the north gate and sent to the province at the same time.

Nantong 91

Sentenced to Death for Murder in Property Dispute

Liu Jingui, a farmer from Baishudun, had no children. His nephew, Liu Mingming, was designated as his heir. Subsequently, Liu Jingui also brought in Liu Mingrong as his son-in-law, and a distribution agreement was drawn up. Liu Mingming was resentful. When Liu Jingui died, Liu Mingming, suspecting that he had left behind a large sum of money, conspired with Cao Er, Zhang Yinchang, Zhu Decheng, and others to kill Liu Mingrong and his wife at night, robbing them of the distribution agreement and money. The case was exposed, and Liu Mingming and his accomplices were apprehended and handed over to the court. On the 25th, after the prosecutor concluded his investigation, Liu Mingming and the others were charged with robbery and murder and were recommended for the death penalty. A public prosecution was initiated.

Water Police District Prepares to Protect Fishing

The fishing season is approaching in various areas along the coast north of the Yangtze River in Jiangsu Province. The provincial government has instructed each team of the Third Water Police District to be responsible for protecting fishing activities. Patrol boats are currently being prepared, and the district headquarters has scheduled a fishing protection meeting for March 10th.

Yangzhou 92

Monk of Fazang Temple Accuses Others of Occupying Temple

Dingyi, the abbot of Fazang Temple in the Fifth District of Jiangdu, claimed that Wan Xiumo, Wan Xingsan, Wan Longji, and three other local villagers forcibly leased out the temple to neighboring villages to open an oil mill, earning a rent of 500 yuan. He hired lawyer Liu Jin in the city to file a lawsuit against the three for robbery and occupation with the Jiangdu District Court's Criminal Division. The court hearing was held on the 24th, and the presiding judge summoned the plaintiff's representative, Runzhi (abbot of Chongning Temple), lawyer Liu Jin, defendants Wan Xiumo and others' lawyer Shu Guozhang, and witnesses Yu Zhongming, Wang Delin, and others. After a detailed two-hour hearing, each side presented their arguments. The judge instructed both parties to submit relevant evidence for further examination and adjudication.

Rice and Vegetables Very Expensive at Heaven Bless University

Continuous spring snow in Yangzhou has caused rice prices to skyrocket, with a risk of shortages. Unexpectedly, snow began to fall again at dusk on the 24th. As night fell, the north wind roared, and the snow intensified. By dusk on the 25th, it had not stopped. The snow depth in deep areas reached six inches. Rice prices suddenly increased by 50 cents, with top-quality rice reaching over ten yuan. Expensive vegetables, such as bok choy, were selling for 200 cash per pound and were still difficult to purchase. If the weather does not clear up soon, there will be a rice shortage, and vegetables will also be exhausted.

Zhenjiang 93

Planning to Establish Public Slaughterhouse

The Provincial Capital Sanitation Office noted that butchers in the provincial capital often slaughtered pigs and sheep inside meat shops, on sidewalks, or in their homes. This caused noise in the early morning and blood to flow freely, creating a foul odor. The office considered this situation detrimental to the city's appearance and a significant hindrance to public health. The office plans to raise funds to establish a public slaughterhouse, which the Sanitation Office will help manage. Butchers in the provincial capital will then be able to slaughter pigs and sheep within the slaughterhouse. This will benefit both the city's appearance and public health. The office sent a letter to the Zhenjiang Meat Industry Association for consultation. If the association agrees, it will send representatives to negotiate. The office will then solicit bids from businesses to operate the slaughterhouse.

Registering People Seeking Employment

The Zhenjiang Chamber of Commerce recognizes that many businesses are failing and the social economy is depressed. The number of unemployed people is increasing daily. The Chamber plans to hold a registration for unemployed people and create a job placement service to compile statistics on commercial talent and provide introductions to jobs, hoping to reduce unemployment and promote social stability. The Chamber's Executive Committee has decided to task the Standing Committee with quickly drafting measures to prepare and implement this plan.

Chongde 94

Large Sum Stolen from Farmers' Bank

A large theft occurred at the local Farmers' Bank late the other night. The bank employees were all asleep upstairs and did not notice anything. The next day they discovered that the safe deposit box had been damaged. Upon opening it, they found that over one thousand yuan in paper money and silver dollars, as well as pledged gold jewelry, had all been stolen. Several pounds of silverware remained. The bank manager, You Qingmi, reported the incident to the county government and investigation authorities, who came to examine the scene. The incident has caused widespread rumors throughout the city, and the public is quite suspicious. The bank's funds are the hard-earned money of farmers. In addition to reporting to the provincial authorities for review, the county government has placed the entire staff under surveillance pending further investigation.

Two Robberies in Beixiang

The home of Qiu Yujing, a traditional Chinese medicine practitioner in Tianren Village, was robbed the other day by multiple bandits who scaled the high walls and stole two chests of clothes and nine quilts, worth approximately over three hundred yuan. At the same time, over ten bandits robbed the home of He Achang, a fisherman from Dingshilanzhen Beihui Yuyang. They brazenly robbed him at gunpoint, searching the bottom of the boat's hold and stealing three hundred yuan in legal tender. He Achang was also severely beaten by the bandits.

Jiaxing 96

Station Porter Arrested for Transporting Opium

The Jiaxing County Security Brigade received a tip on the 25th that over 500 ounces of opium would be transported from Shanghai to Jiaxing in boxes and copper containers. They dispatched investigators to wait at the station. Around 2 p.m., they saw a porter carrying a bedroll, followed by two policemen, leaving the station towards the Oriental Hotel area. The investigators, together with police officers from the Public Security Bureau, apprehended the porter. The two policemen left. The investigators opened the porter's bedroll and found 112 packages of opium, consisting of Yunnan and Sichuan opium, each weighing one ounce. The porter and the opium were sent to the First Branch of the Public Security Bureau. After interrogation, the porter identified himself as Chen Xiaozhao. He was subjected to a strict interrogation, but he did not reveal the source and destination of the opium. He is still being questioned.

Ningbo 97

Group Wedding Date Set in Cixi

The Cixi County government has been preparing for a new lifestyle group wedding. Since the registration began, many people have registered. The certificates and all the procedures are ready. The date is set for March 1st at the Minglun Hall in the school palace.

County-Wide General Inspection for Opium Addiction

The registration of opium addicts in Yin County ended on the 25th. The Yin County government and the Ningbo Public Security Bureau, to eliminate the remaining opium, will conduct a county-wide general inspection for opium addiction, starting on the 26th. The urban area inspection will last until the 29th, and the rural area inspection will last until March 10th. All opium addicts, whether they have quit, are quitting, or are selling opium, and their residences, will be inspected. Opium addicts who voluntarily surrender and destroy their opium and paraphernalia beforehand will be exempted from punishment. Those whose opium and paraphernalia are discovered during the inspection will be arrested and prosecuted without leniency.

Local News

Two British Flying Boats Arrive in Shanghai Under Supervision This Afternoon Arrived at 2:05 PM Scheduled to Leave Shanghai for Japan on the 29th 98

The British Royal Air Force, for the purpose of visiting China and Japan, specifically sent three flying boats led by Smith, the commander of the British Far East Air Force, departing from Singapore. Due to weather conditions along the way, the journey was repeatedly delayed. One boat, number four, was left in Xiamen for repairs due to engine damage and will not be able to continue the journey. The remaining two boats, numbers two and three, departed from Xiamen on the 24th. Due to unfavorable weather conditions, they were forced to land near Nanguan in Wenzhou. They took off from Wenzhou this morning at 10:05 AM and flew to Shanghai, landing at 2:05 PM this afternoon in front of the Zhoujiazui Island fish market in Yangshupu. They are scheduled to leave Shanghai for Japan on the 29th. The details are as follows:

Welcoming Personnel The British Embassy's Aviation Counselor's Office received news this morning that the two boats had left Wenzhou, immediately notifying all relevant parties by telephone. Zhoujiazui Island, which had been quiet, suddenly became bustling with traffic and excitement. Those who went to welcome the boats included Zhang Tingrong, representing Mayor Wu of our municipal government; Fan Wei of the Garrison Command; Hong Qi of the Public Security Bureau; Wen Changzhao of the Shanghai Flying Station; Aviation Commissioners Liu Fangxiu, Yang Guanyu, and Qin Zongshen; Wang Zhinan of the Municipal Security Office; Mr. Winock of the British Embassy's Aviation Counselor's Office; Mr. Fowles of the British Royal Aeronautical Society; Commander Iida of the Japanese Third Fleet Aircraft; Mr. Ashino Hiro of the Japanese Embassy's Intelligence Department; Mr. Yanagi and Mr. Hashizume of the Japanese Embassy; Mr. Walter of De Hansa Company; Mr. Gabaru of the Italian Embassy's Aviation Counselor's Office; Mr. Li Jingcong, General Manager of Eurasia Aviation Corporation; and over two hundred other guests.

The photo shows British flying boats numbers two and three moored in the Huangpu River (taken by International News Agency)

Landing Details Prior to the arrival, the Public Security Bureau dispatched a police team, and the Water Police Bureau also sent a water police team to maintain order at the scene. The Jianghai Customs Security Office also dispatched several small launches to greet the boats. Asia Petroleum Company also sent the Dian Guang small launch to the port for supply purposes. At 1:20 PM, the two flying boats suddenly appeared at the east corner of the Huangpu River, and the crowd craned their necks to look. The two aircraft flew west, one after the other, circling Shanghai once. After a short while, they turned back towards the fish market. The engine sound roared, and the aircraft circled the fish market once before gradually descending. Boat number two was in front, and boat number three was behind, landing in the river west of Zhoujiazui Island and mooring at the designated buoy. The landing was completed at 2:00 PM.

Reception by Various Parties Jianghai's Jinghui and Guang small launches, as well as the Security Office's security launches, all sailed to the river to greet the boats. The Aviation Administration also sent an aircraft to welcome the boats in the air. Zhang Tingrong, Winock, and others took the Hongmin small launch, towing two sampans, to welcome the boats. Commander Smith disembarked and went to the Jiao City Market to rest and meet with the welcoming personnel, offering them beer. He then went to the Cathay Hotel for rest. That evening, the British Chamber of Commerce and the embassy hosted a banquet in a private capacity. Due to the mourning period for King George of England, the event was kept simple. Tomorrow, from 5:00 PM to 7:00 PM, Mayor Wu Tiecheng will host a tea party at his private residence.

Personnel Arriving in Shanghai The personnel who arrived in Shanghai yesterday included Commander Smith, team leader Scott, and officials Stewart, McLeay, Van Leichey, Lloyd, and Piper (on boat number two); Brighton, Rickert, Hunt, Holopen, Jimmis, Gibson, Warren, Stamfordley, and Howells (on boat number three), totaling sixteen people.

Reception for Reporters Commander Smith held a press conference at the Cathay Hotel, Room 533, at 5:00 PM yesterday, making the following remarks: "I am leading the British Royal Air Force flying boats on a visit to China and Japan. After arriving in Hong Kong, we were delayed for several days due to weather conditions, as you already know. We left Xiamen at 10:00 AM on the 24th. We were forced to land in Nanguan due to rain, staying for two nights (spending the first night on the boat). We were still blocked on the next day. We finally took off at 10:05 AM this morning (the 26th). Nanguan is a small place, but the scenery is picturesque. We also received hospitality from the local authorities there. The plane left in Xiamen has a damaged engine that will take time to repair. After it is finished, it will fly directly to Hong Kong. If the weather is good tomorrow morning, the 29th, we will fly to Kagoshima, south of Kyushu, Japan. We plan to fly from Kashima to Xia Pu next Monday, then to Tokyo, staying for four days. Then we will fly back to Kagoshima, and return to Singapore via Shanghai. I am deeply grateful to the Shanghai Municipal Government, the Fish Market Department of the Ministry of Industry, and the Public Security Bureau of Jianghai Customs for their hospitality and various conveniences." Smith then answered reporters' questions, "I am the commander of the Far East Air Force, which includes Singapore and Hong Kong. The force consists of three groups, one group has four flying boats, two reserve boats, and the other two groups have twelve aircraft each." Smith reportedly participated in the European War and took office as the Far East Commander in 1933.

Flying Boat Equipment The flying boats that came to China this time were manufactured by the oldest British company, Short Brothers, and are suitable for flying over the sea. The boats are silver-gray and equipped with two engines, each with 560 horsepower. The durable cruising range is 2,350 miles, at an altitude of 2,000 feet, with a maximum speed of 145 miles per hour and an average speed of 105 miles per hour. The bow is equipped with gun positions and machine guns. The front of the cabin has two driver's seats, the middle is the pilot's seat, and there are also mechanic and radio operator seats, as well as cooking and storage facilities. The equipment is very complete.

Flying Route The three British flying boats left Singapore at 7:00 AM on the 10th of this month, arriving in Kuching at 11:30 AM that day. They left Kuching at 7:00 AM on the 12th and arrived in Kudat at 2:30 PM that afternoon. They left Kudat at 6:00 AM on the 13th and arrived in Manila at 1:00 PM. The third boat, due to engine damage, flew directly to Xiamen on the 19th. They left Manila on the 16th and arrived in Hong Kong at 1:30 PM that afternoon. They were delayed in Hong Kong for several days due to bad weather. On the morning of the 23rd at 9:30 AM, they left Hong Kong and arrived in Xiamen at 1:14 PM. After arriving in Xiamen, the fourth boat was left in Xiamen for repairs due to engine damage, and was unable to continue. The remaining two boats left Xiamen for Shanghai at 10:10 AM on the 24th. They were forced to land near Wenzhou due to fog. They flew from Wenzhou to Shanghai at 10:05 AM yesterday morning.

Foreign Press Reports The Greater Shanghai Evening Post reported that the two British flying boats took off from Nanguan, Wenzhou, at 10:00 AM this morning (the 26th) and arrived safely in Shanghai at 2:50 PM this afternoon, mooring near the fishing market at Zhoujiazui. They plan to stay for two days. It is said that the weather between Wenzhou and Shanghai was good this morning, overcast and calm. The six officers on board are staying at the Cathay Hotel, and the remaining ten are lodging on the Asia Petroleum Company's riverboat, Dianguang, moored at the New Fish Market pier. Because today is within the British national mourning period for King George, all receptions are informal. The two flying boats will fly to Japan after staying in Shanghai for two full days. The third flying boat is still stranded in Xiamen, awaiting the spare parts needed for repairs. All three flying boats are the Singapore Third-style, designed for long-distance sea reconnaissance. The crew can stay in the aircraft for several weeks. Each aircraft is equipped with four engines, with a maximum speed of 145 miles per hour and a cruising speed of 105 miles per hour. They can fly 3,000 miles in one stretch.

Beijing-Yunnan Flight Test Aircraft Arrives in Yunnan This Afternoon Arrived Safely in Kunming at 1:50 PM 99

Huadong News Agency reported that the Eurasia Aviation Corporation's newly opened Beijing-Yunnan route had been fully prepared, and the company sent its first giant aircraft, a Junkers Ju 52, from Shanghai for a test flight on the morning of the 25th. It arrived at the Chengdu station at 4:50 PM that afternoon for an overnight stay. Yesterday morning at 10:05 AM, it continued its test flight from Chengdu. A reporter from the Huadong News Agency called the Eurasia Corporation's Longhua Telegraph Office at 7:30 PM last night. According to the report, the aircraft sent a telegram reporting its departure after leaving at 10:05 AM yesterday morning. The company's deputy head of the Aircraft and Navigation Group, He En; head of the Operations Group, Liao Guanxuan; director of the Xi'an station, Yang Xingzhong; and telegraph operator Xu Tiemin also accompanied the aircraft. At 6:00 PM, a second telegram was received stating that the aircraft had safely landed in Kunming, Yunnan, at 1:50 PM that afternoon. It passed through Guiyang along the way but did not land. The total flight time was two hours and forty-five minutes, with excellent results. The aircraft will stay there today for inspection. It is scheduled to leave Kunming tomorrow morning (the 28th) and fly back to the capital via Changsha and Nanchang.

Japanese Ambassador Arita Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday Delivers Written Statement To Establish Amicable Relations Between the Two Countries Both Sides Should Accurately Recognize the Situation and Implement the Most Appropriate Adjustments 100

Central News Agency reported that the newly appointed Japanese Ambassador to China, Hachiro Arita, arrived in Shanghai yesterday afternoon at 2:30 PM, with his wife, Counselor of the Embassy Kutsuchi, Army Attaché Major General Isogai, Secretary Kondo, and five other people on the Japanese ship Asama Maru. The ship docked at the Whangpoo Wharf, where representatives from various Chinese and Japanese circles welcomed them. After disembarking, the Japanese Ambassador returned to the Ambassador's residence on Bi Xun Road to rest. The date of presenting his credentials in Nanjing will be determined after the Chinese government approves the date. The details are as follows:

Welcoming Personnel The Asama Maru was originally scheduled to arrive in Shanghai at 3:00 PM yesterday, but because it encountered a tailwind, it arrived at the Whangpoo Wharf at 2:30 PM. Those who came to welcome the ambassador from various Chinese and Japanese circles included the newly appointed Chinese Ambassador to Japan, Xu Shiying; Secretary Tang Shixuan, representing Mayor Wu Tiecheng; Commissioner Wang Changchun; Director Zhou Jue of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' Shanghai Office; former Minister of Interior Xu Xiuzhi; and from the Japanese side, Counselor of the Embassy Wakasugi Kanyei, Counselor Ashino Hiro, Arino Manabu, Motono, Hagiwara, Naval Attaché Sato, Kondo Kusano, Military Attaché stationed in Nanjing Nakahara, Army Attaché Oki, Utsunomiya, Consul General stationed in Nanjing Suma, Consul General stationed in Shanghai Ishii, Consul Sugihara, Police Chief Kamihata, head of the Civil Group Kaneno, chairman of the Civil Group Conference Hishida, president of the Chamber of Commerce Yoneri, and dozens of others. At the same time, the Public Concession Police Force also dispatched detectives to the wharf to maintain security.

Arita's Demeanor Ambassador Arita was wearing a formal suit yesterday. He met with each of the welcoming personnel on the ship, shaking hands and expressing his gratitude. He is currently 53 years old. He graduated from the Faculty of Law of Tokyo Imperial University in 1909 and then joined the Ministry of Foreign Affairs as Vice Consul in Fengtian. After that, he served as Consul, Foreign Affairs Officer, First Secretary of the Legation, and First Secretary of the Embassy, Consul General, and other positions in places such as Chicago, Ottawa, Honolulu, and Siam. While serving as First Secretary of the Embassy in Washington, D.C., he attended the Washington Naval Conference as the secretary-general of the Japanese delegation. He later served as Vice Consul in Tianjin, Minister to Germany, Director of the Asian Affairs Bureau, and Minister Plenipotentiary to Hungary. In May 1932, he took office as Foreign Minister, and in 1933, he served as Ambassador to Belgium.

Written Statement After arriving in Shanghai, Ambassador Arita immediately released a written statement to the press, translated as follows: "I have served in the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for many years. Twenty-five years ago, I served in Fengtian. Since then, I have worked in Beijing and Tianjin. In the Ministry, I served as Director of the Asian Affairs Bureau and as Minister, and have always been in charge of matters relating to China. This time I have been appointed to China, as if returning to my second home. The establishment of amicable relations between Japan and China is an absolute requirement for the peace and prosperity of East Asia. This is recognized by the people of both countries. At this time of crisis, it is admirable to seek a way to manage it well. And I deeply respect the hard work of my predecessor, Ambassador Ariyoshi. To establish amicable relations between the two countries, it is necessary for both sides to accurately recognize the real situation and implement the most appropriate adjustments. To achieve this goal, I sincerely hope to follow the policy of my government and do my best. However, I have been in Europe for more than two years, and I am somewhat estranged from matters relating to East Asia. As I take office, I will listen carefully to the opinions of officials and civilians from all sectors of both countries, and at the same time, I will carefully observe the situation in China and make appropriate adjustments, so as to avoid any regrets. This is what I sincerely pray for."

Ice Outside Dagu Gradually Loosening Huizhou and Other Ships Escape Danger Can Arrive in Shanghai Tomorrow Ice Floes Gradually Loosening 102

The ice floes outside Dagu have gradually loosened due to slightly warmer weather. The frozen sea surface has been broken up by icebreakers hired by the Tianjin Customs and Port Authority. Several ships blocked outside the Dagu lightship have been able to escape with the help of the icebreakers. The British merchant Taikoo Company's Huizhou ship, which had been frozen in the ice for a month, was rescued by the Xin Shengjing ship for the first time, but was frozen again. Today, the Shanghai office received a telegram saying that it has left the Dagu ice layer and can arrive in Shanghai tomorrow. The Hunan, which has also been blocked by ice for a long time, has also escaped at the same time and will arrive one day later than the Huizhou. Other ships are currently being rescued. Although the sea route is not fully open, it is generally possible to supply food and beverages to those within the lightship area. It is said that a portion of the ice-blocked ships is expected to escape within a day or two.

Brief Articles of Association of the Shanghai Goods Relief Association

The passed brief articles of association of the Shanghai Goods Relief Association are as follows: Article 1: The Shanghai Fundraising Association for Flood Relief in Various Provinces, for the purpose of raising flood relief funds, solicits goods and issues gift coupons, named the Shanghai Goods Relief Association. Article 2: The gift coupons issued by this association are exclusively for those who donate to disaster relief, called Fortune Fruit Coupons. The donated funds will be used as spring relief funds by the Shanghai Fundraising Association for Flood Relief in Various Provinces. Article 3: In addition to the real estate, jewelry, and valuables donated by Ms. Yao, a resident of Suzhou, introduced by Mr. Nie Yuntai and designated for relief in northern Jiangsu, and the fields donated by Mr. Tang Mufen of Beiping, introduced by Mr. Cheng Jingsheng and designated for relief in northern Jiangsu, as the foundation, this association will seek additional supplements to ensure that each coupon has a gift. Article 4: The categories of goods solicited by this association are as follows: Real estate, gold and stone, calligraphy and painting, books and stationery, clothing, collectibles, fine art and handicrafts, domestic products, refined foods, and all other supplies. Article 5: The places where this association should solicit goods are as follows: Major companies and stores, major factories, product organizations, collectors, contemporary famous calligraphers and painters, enthusiastic philanthropists, and others. Article 6: The methods for this association to solicit goods are as follows: Advertising in newspapers, sending letters of solicitation, door-to-door solicitation. Article 7: This association handles. Article 8: The Shanghai Fundraising Association for Flood Relief in Various Provinces will nominate fifteen members, who will mutually elect nine standing committee members, and further elect one chairman to attend meetings regularly and preside over association affairs. Article 9: The office of this association will be headed by a director and two deputy directors mutually elected by the standing committee, and will have several staff members responsible for receiving and dispatching, storing, displaying, publicizing, soliciting donations, handling documents, accounting, and general affairs, all of whom will be decided upon, hired, or employed by this association. Article 10: This association will establish a supervisory committee, consisting of nine members mutually elected from the directors and supervisors of the Shanghai Fundraising Association for Flood Relief in Various Provinces, to supervise association affairs. Article 11: The goods solicited by this association, except for commodities with fixed prices and calligraphy and paintings by famous people with published prices, do not need to be evaluated separately. Those that must be priced should be evaluated separately by experts hired by this association. Article 12: The goods solicited by this association will be displayed and exhibited. The exhibition rules will be determined separately. Article 13: The maximum value of the gifts is 20,000 yuan, with subsequent reductions. The grading of the gifts will be decided by the committee. The fundraising target is 12,000 coupons. From the date of establishment of this association, those who donate 10 yuan will receive two coupons, and more will be given in proportion. However, for donations that have already been given Fortune Fruit Coupons, no separate receipt will be issued. Article 14: The office of this association is located in Shanghai. Article 15: The committee meetings of this association are not fixed. They will be convened periodically by the chairman and standing committee members. The standing committee meetings are tentatively scheduled to be held once a week on Saturday afternoons at 4 p.m. In case of special matters, extraordinary standing committee meetings may be convened by the chairman or standing committee members. Article 16: When necessary, staff meetings may be convened by the director. Article 17: All receipts and expenditures of this association should be handled by specialists borrowed from banks to ensure prudence. Article 18: Women and gentlemen who donate goods will be thanked daily in the newspapers by this association and should be given appropriate awards by the National Government by the Shanghai Fundraising Association for Flood Relief in Various Provinces, in accordance with the donation and disaster relief incentive measures. Article 19: After the completion of this association's work, a report on the association's work should be compiled. Article 20: These brief articles of association will be implemented from the date of approval by the Shanghai Fundraising Association for Flood Relief Committee. Article 21: If there are any matters not covered in these brief articles of association, they may be proposed for amendment by the committee.
