Shen Bao National Products Special Issue

Opening Remarks 182

— Yang An

National crisis is not terrifying; saving the nation has a great path. The whole country, old and young, all wear national cloth.

This is a saying by the Party-state elder Mr. Wu. Mr. Wu believes that wearing domestically produced cotton cloth is a great path to saving the nation. This is a penetrating remark worth remembering by everyone. Not long ago, newspapers reported that the new British emperor went to that market to visit. He bought some domestically produced clothing and personally told the people, "I really like to use the products of our own factories. I hope everyone will consistently use British goods in the future. This is the most glorious thing." Have you seen any Europeans or Japanese who do not wear clothing made from their own country's materials? Sometimes they even proudly say to us, "Why do your countrymen like to wear foreign fabrics? You clearly have excellent silk and satin, but why don't you use them? What is the mentality?" I felt angry and ashamed when I heard this, and I believe that wearing foreign goods is indeed a great disgrace to the Chinese people. In the past, we could say that domestically produced fabrics did not have excellent products yet. Now, thanks to the efforts of many domestic goods factories, all products can be said to be comparable to foreign goods, if not better. Facts speak louder than words. If you go to domestic goods companies and domestic cloth factories to observe, you will know the amazing progress of domestically produced cotton cloth in recent years. This publication is specially publishing a special issue to draw the attention of the Chinese people.

Domestically Produced Cotton Cloth Worth Promoting 183

— Xuan Wan

Clothing is a representation of a person, so the suitability of a person's clothing is very much representative of their own excellent character. In ancient times, people wore simple cloth garments and plain silk hats. Like Han Wengong's lifelong wearing of cloth garments and Jing Jiang's virtue continuing even after her son became noble, these examples show us how virtuous men and good mothers in our country's past history adopted simple clothing, lived a simple life, and strived for the future of the nation and the people.

However, with the evolution of history and the spread of European and American customs after our country opened up to the world, the so-called modern men and women developed luxurious habits. They not only greatly changed the style of clothing, adopting Western suits and qipao dresses, but also mostly used foreign goods in terms of materials, firmly establishing a psychology of loving imported goods. We only need to look at the shocking amount of import surplus in recent years, the large-scale import of foreign woolens and silk fabrics into China, and on the other hand, the constant cries of distress from our original cotton and silk industries, to know the severity of this disaster, which threatens the economic lifeline of our entire nation, promotes the main cause of poverty among our country's poor people, and the crisis of national ruin and family destruction is about to unfold before us.

Therefore, I dare to say with conviction that the prerequisite for our adoption of clothing at the current stage must be domestic production. Moreover, under the increasingly acute economic panic and sluggish market, we should pay attention to the simplicity and frugality of clothing, and it is worth promoting the use of domestically produced cotton cloth to make clothing. As far as I know, the cotton fabrics of companies like Sanyou Industrial Society, Hongxin Dyeing and Weaving Factory, and Sanxin Dyeing and Weaving Factory are of excellent quality. Whether used to tailor long gowns, qipaos, Western suits, or student uniforms, they are very elegant and beautiful, and durable and wrinkle-resistant. Compared with expensive foreign goods, they are also quite comparable, but in terms of price, they can be much cheaper. At this time when our country's economic future hangs by a thread, how can we continue to act as foreign goods promoters and not fulfill the duty of a citizen for the future of domestic goods!

Let us shout loudly! May everyone work together to promote the domestically produced cotton cloth movement.

Talking About Nantong Coarse Cloth 184

— Qiao Yunxun

Nantong County is as famous as the model province of Shanxi. It is a well-known industrial area. Therefore, of course, talented people come from such a blessed land. This model reputation was created single-handedly by Mr. Zhang Jian, whose education, industry, municipal administration, transportation, and water conservancy all surpassed other counties. There is a cause and then there is an effect. The word "model" was truly worthy of Nantong during its heyday. In fact, its "Nantong coarse cloth" originated very early, not after Mr. Zhang retired to the forest and worked hard to rebuild Nantong. It was originally a famous cotton-producing area in various provinces. "Domestically produced cotton cloth" had the widest sales and the longest history of weaving. "Nantong coarse cloth" seems to have no equal. It is a widespread rural side business. A few thatched cottages, two wooden looms, no fixed working hours, no consumption of workers and employees. Every village woman and every country girl in the county has the skill of spinning and weaving. To what extent is it promoted? Can you eat? Can you defecate? If you can eat and defecate, there is no one who cannot spin and weave. This custom spread from Nantong to Haimen and affected Rugao. Therefore, Tonghai coarse cloth and Rugao blue cloth are called together. In the past, the width of the fabric was narrow, but now it has been widened, making it most suitable for making quilt linings, short shirts, and shorts. It is strong, durable, and easy to wash, unparalleled in its kind. In the northern Jiangsu provinces of Jiangsu Province, it is still the custom to buy some "Tongzhou coarse cloth" and "Rugao blue cloth" when marrying a daughter. In recent years, in order to cater to the trend, patterned fabrics are also woven. Since the loss of the Northeast, a large number of goods exported through the customs have been reduced, but Fujian and Guangdong still have resident water merchants who set up shops to collect them. It is said that the warp yarn is currently made from factory products, and the weft yarn is still spun by hand. The success of a cloth lies in its sturdiness. It is faintly heard that Mr. Jian wore coarse cloth shirts and trousers throughout his life and instructed his son Xiaoruo on his deathbed to make the inner lining of his quilt entirely from coarse cloth, with only the outer garment being the ceremonial dress of the Minister of Agriculture and Commerce. The agricultural and mining bureaus of other provinces often send commissioners to Tong to purchase cotton seeds every year. I stayed in Tong for a short time some years ago and witnessed rural women carrying cloth to the shops for sale early in the morning, waiting by the door before the shops opened. As for Shanghai-Yangtze River steamships, when they arrive in Tongzhou, there are vendors selling Tongzhou coarse cloth on both trips. If this skill penetrates every township and village, how could the rural economy be bankrupt? If the sales organization is perfect, Nantong coarse cloth can take the top spot in domestically produced cotton cloth. Spinning, weaving, and sales should also be spread throughout the provinces. Then, will our "cotton cloth market" allow anyone else to intervene?

My Little Experience in Wearing Domestically Produced Cotton Cloth 185

— Man Bin

Ten years ago, an exhibition of domestically produced cotton cloth was held at Mr. Shi Liangcai's residence, sponsored by Sanyou Industrial Society. More than a dozen schools attended that day, as well as fifty or sixty ladies and young ladies, all wearing domestically produced clothing. After everyone discussed it, they agreed that the tailoring of clothes should have five conditions: first, domestically produced; second, simple; third, strong; fourth, economical; and fifth, beautiful. At that time, the principals of various schools agreed to these five conditions for selecting clothes for students. One principal did not agree with "beautiful," but because it was not limited to school uniforms, this condition was ultimately added. From then on, I always adhered to this principle when making clothes for myself and my children. Sometimes, when the school authorities bought non-domestic goods or domestic goods in disguise, I would personally go to the school and argue with them. I often said that if schools are unwilling to sincerely use domestic goods when making school uniforms, what is the point of talking about patriotism and saving the nation? Recently, because my children have grown up and I have nothing to do, I often go to various schools to take a look and, by the way, persuade them to choose school uniforms and pay attention to genuine domestically produced cotton cloth. Sometimes, I honestly and bluntly give them many samples, advising them not to be fooled, so as not to disappoint the many families who love to use domestic goods in your schools. At the same time, I visit many families to persuade them to wear domestic fabrics. When I married off my daughter last year, almost all the clothes in her dowry were made of domestic fabrics. Sanyou Society and Hongxin Factory are my old customers, and Mr. Xu Yangnan also served as my consultant. I visit the Chinese National Goods Company, which sells fabrics from Hongxin, Dafeng, Sanxin, and other factories, every week. Recently, I often visit the third-floor market of Sanyou Society, believing it is a responsibility that our women should have. The funniest thing is that my eight-year-old daughter always asks if it is from Mr. Xu or Mr. Wan's factory every time she decides to wear new clothes, because she always hears her older sister telling her that our family's clothes are purchased from Hongxin or Sanyou. Even more amusing, my eleven-year-old daughter always refuses when the school makes school uniforms for her and insists that I personally choose them for her. Children are the most innocent and naive. The idea that they will not buy anything but domestic goods is very strong in their little minds, and they will never be careless. Yesterday, my niece hosted a full moon celebration for her newborn child. When I went to her house, I saw that seventy to eighty percent of the baby clothes on display were products of domestic factories. Everyone praised her patriotism, believing that it is important to cultivate the habit of using domestic goods from a young age. I still remember that the Joint Production and Sales Association initiated the Domestic Goods Wearing Association. Of the 108 women who attended, more than half, or more than 60, wore domestic cotton fabrics, and 40 wore domestic silk and satin. It can be said that foreign fabrics were completely absent that day. Even if someone wore them, they would feel ashamed and uneasy. From this point of view, the future of Chinese domestic goods is very promising.

Domestically Produced Cotton Cloth Worn by Our Women 186

— Ms. Ju Ju

My reason for wearing cotton cloth probably dates back to before I got married. At that time, domestic cotton cloth was already very popular. Even though some of us women also used imported foreign cloth, most of our female compatriots were already able to wear domestically produced cotton cloth. For example, the same qipao dress, those made of foreign cloth were only worn by the fashionable wives, grandmothers, and young ladies. Most of the women in our lower and middle classes wore those made of domestically produced cotton cloth. I remember when I was young, when my mother was alive, our brothers and sisters all wore clothes made of domestically produced cotton cloth, and we all liked them. My mother also said, "Clothes made of cotton cloth can be worn for several years because the cloth is durable and the quality is durable, and at the same time, it is cheap. So we love to use it. If you don't mind, you might as well continue to make cotton clothes for your children..." Now, when I think back to these words, they still ring in my ears.

Later, due to the intrusion of foreign cloth, cotton cloth was gradually eliminated. All the families who spun and wove their own cloth gave up because foreign cloth was cheaper. As a result, women all wore clothes made of foreign cloth, but I still followed my mother's teachings. The clothes I wear, the clothes my children wear, and the clothes used by the whole family are all made of cotton cloth produced by Sanyou Industrial Society, Hongxin, Sanxin, and other factories. Therefore, my classmates said, "You are really a practitioner of promoting domestic goods. How many people in our country are willing to wear cotton cloth and use cotton cloth like you?" But in my opinion, cotton cloth is indeed more durable and wear-resistant than foreign cloth!

Impressions of Coarse Cloth and Rural Farmers 187

— Meng Zhao

Speaking of coarse cloth, I can't help but think of the old farmer who comes wearing coarse cloth clothes, floating like a legend!

The old farmer has a long beard reaching his chest and still works at sunrise and rests at sunset! Full of energy! From head to toe, he wears nothing but coarse cloth: a black cloth hat, a blue cloth robe, white cloth socks, and his feet are firmly on the ground, working hard! Really working hard! Growing grains of rice like pearls for those who do not know the hardships of farming to enjoy. He often warns his descendants: "When eating a bowl of porridge or a bowl of rice, think of where it came from! When using half a thread, always remember the difficulty of obtaining materials!"

In the past, the countryside was full of the sound of looms. The so-called "men plow and women weave" was submerged by the dumping of imported cotton cloth! The craft of weaving coarse cloth in the countryside was eliminated! And the looms were left empty! "Click, click, and click again, Mulan is weaving at the door. No sound of looms is heard? Only the woman's sigh is heard!" It seems to be a portrait of today's world for thousands of years to come!

Rural farmers, weaving their own coarse cloth, have very narrow widths! During the farming gap, rural women and farmers often piled it on their shoulders and went out to sell it door to door. My mother liked to buy it to make undershirts and cloth socks for me. Nowadays, the cotton cloth of Shanghai National Goods Cloth Factory has better shapes and colors, and of course it is welcomed by the public.

The reporter recalls the simplicity and frugality of rural farmers wearing coarse cloth! If everyone imitated the rural farmers wearing coarse cloth (like the old farmer mentioned above) and wore coarse cloth for life, the country would be saved without the need for saving!

Song to Persuade the Use of Domestic Goods 188

— Qing Qu

Don't beat the drum, don't beat the gong. Listen to me sing a song about domestic goods. China's civilization started the earliest. Creation has always been abundant. Thinking back, Xuanyuan was the Yellow Emperor. Tracing back, there were the Three Sovereigns and Fuxi. Past events can still be known in detail. They first drew the Eight Trigrams and created writing. They tied nets and taught farming and fishing. They also raised sacrifices to fill the kitchen. All kinds of creations started from this. Everyone lived happily and peacefully. In ancient times, clothes were made of silk and hemp. The four seasons were dressed without extravagance. Raising silkworms and processing silk was the work of Lei Zu. Even as the emperor's consort, she also washed silk. Cotton is said to have come from India. China today has coarse cloth. Suitable for spring, summer, and winter. Farming is only for this duty. It has been beneficial for thousands of years. The colors are as beautiful as brocade. Therefore, the cotton is ginned and woven. The women's work is to rub the floss and pull the cotton. Unexpectedly, after the opening of the five ports. Foreigners forced and enticed us. Imported goods filled the market. They seized our money and did not let go. Try flipping through the customs record books. The leakage is endless year after year. A piece of clothing or a pair of shoes may be small. But they are all the people's cream and fat. Therefore, I sincerely advise. Domestic goods are the treasure of the country. At this time of poverty and exhaustion. Awakening everyone should be early. The prosperity of the market relies on farmers and workers. The first is frugality and most elegant. Rejecting foreign goods is not difficult. Just need effort and unity of heart. From then on, all industries can rise again. The country will be rich and the army will be strong. Gentlemen, keep this in mind. It is the ambition of a patriotic man.

Commercial News

Finance High-Volume Transactions: Intense Competition for Covering Short Positions 191

Spot Market Drys Up, Prices Surge by Two Yuan and Ten Cents; Bulls Outnumber Bears by Forty

Yesterday, the gold market initially saw a slight decline due to downstream demand for pure gold. However, it managed to maintain stability as major players took advantage of the lower prices to purchase bars. Subsequently, short sellers rushed to cover their positions, and major players also entered the market. The spot market dried up, leading to a rapid rebound in prices. Early in the morning, overseas silver markets showed a contraction in London and stability in the US. Floor traders claimed that India would continue to purchase at listed prices after the market closed, with a lack of supply supporting the market. The forward price of silver in Montreux fell by between one and two and nine-tenths of a cent. Exchange rates slightly contracted. London raw gold fell by two pence. The Central Bank's listed prices were announced, showing stability in both the US and the UK. Customs gold units fell by four cents. The standard bid price for gold was listed at 1,145 yuan and two jiao, retreating in over-the-counter pre-market trading due to slight sales by Da De Cheng and Tong Tai Chang, falling to around 45 yuan. The morning opened with a low, slightly declining further, but major players strongly purchased, maintaining stability. Afterwards, the Hong Kong and Shanghai Bank announced listed prices, showing stability in the US and the UK. Foreign exchange banks conducted interbank foreign exchange transactions at par. The gold market also stabilized. Many retail investors were still selling, hovering around 45 yuan, with limited fluctuations. The silver balancing tax was announced, falling by half a cent, but lacking special changes at this point. Later, retail short sellers covered their positions, and major players also made purchases. The spot market dried up, resulting in demand exceeding supply, and rumors intensified, stimulating buying. There was a severe lack of supply, causing a rapid surge in prices. Afterwards, sellers became eager at higher prices, and the afternoon saw a wavering trend. Spot prices for April delivery were five and a half yuan higher for those exiting the market, while March delivery for April was 4.78 jiao higher for short positions. The total number of contracts was over 11,000, with bulls outnumbering bears by forty. The morning market conditions are recorded below.

The morning opening was 1,145 yuan and two jiao, a decrease of nine jiao from the previous close. Shun Mao accepted bars, rising to 5 yuan and three jiao. Ri Chang, Mao Yong, Da De Cheng, and Ying Xiang sold, falling to 4 yuan and a half. Shun Mao, Ri Chang, Tong Tai Chang, Fu Xing Yong took advantage of the low prices to accept bars, rising to 5 yuan and one jiao. Da Fa Yong and Ri Chang divested, retreating to 4 yuan and seven jiao. Fu Xing Yong, Da Chang Xiang, Heng Yu, Zhi Chang, and Hui Xiang all sold, rising back to 5 yuan and three jiao. Da De Cheng, Qing Fa Yong, Ri Chang, and Hui Xiang divested, retreating again to 4 yuan and eight jiao. The Hong Kong and Shanghai Bank announced listed prices, showing stability in the US and the UK, calming sentiment. Shun Mao, Ding Kang, Qia Feng Yong, and Fu Xing Yong advanced to 5 yuan and one jiao. Xiang He sold bars. The silver balancing tax was announced, falling by half a cent, retreating to 4 yuan and eight jiao. Fu Xing Yong, Hong Kang Yong, and Yi Cheng took the opportunity to advance, rising to 5 yuan and one jiao. However, because Ri Chang, Da Feng Heng, and others were divesting, it hovered around 5 yuan for quite a while. Afterwards, retail short sellers, Ri Chang, Heng Chang Yong covered their positions, and major players such as Fu Xing Yong, Jin Feng Yong, Li Feng Hui Xiang, Rui Xing Xiang Feng Yu, Qing Yong Fu Tai Yong, Yuan Mao Yong, Qian Yuan Yong also advanced. The spot market dried up, and rumors fueled buying, gradually rising to 9 yuan and three jiao. Chun Yuan Yong divested at the high price, falling to 8 yuan and seven jiao. Zhi Chang and Da De Cheng were still advancing, rising to 9 yuan and a half. Yarn and Cotton: Affected by the Japanese Political Incident 193

The Downward Trend of Bid Yarn Intensifies

Trading Suspended at Osaka Sampin Market, Panic Among the People; Japanese Merchants Sell Off, Market Situation Further Declines

The yarn market is weakening, and the downward trend is intensifying, due to the poor market atmosphere and the suspension of trading at the Osaka Sampin cotton yarn market, causing panic among the people. The pressure from Japanese merchants selling off is very heavy, with Chang Feng showing a strong intention to sell, causing the market to decline step by step. The July contract broke below the 200 yuan mark. However, although spot yarn is constrained by futures, the selling price has not been significantly affected.

All Months of Bid Yarn Decline. The opening of the bid yarn market in the morning showed a weakening and sluggish state in all months. Due to the suspension of trading at the Osaka Sampin yarn market, panic among the people, and a consistent downward trend in the overseas cotton industry, the market had no support capacity. As a result, all months fell by 3.5.6.7 jiao compared to the previous day's closing price. The opening in the afternoon was still good. After the second round, the extra edition of the Da Mei Evening News spread more and more, and the atmosphere was tense. The Osaka Sampin yarn market still had no news of reopening, causing some selling, so the decline was more severe than in the morning market. According to the market, Japanese merchants came to sell off again, with Chang Feng selling over 2,000 bales in each round, and the market price declined further. US Cotton Continues to Decline in Both Near and Distant Months 197

Government Sells Stockpiled Cotton, Discouraging Sentiment

Yesterday, US cotton opened with fluctuations of 1 to 2 pounds in each month. The news from Liverpool was unfavorable, causing bulls to liquidate. There were some carry-over sales of old cotton, while new cotton saw sales and bullish liquidations in the Far East, causing near-term and distant cotton to decline successively. Afterwards, industry players bought in and short positions covered, leading to a partial recovery. Sentiment was discouraged by the government's sale of stockpiled cotton. The New Cotton Field Bill has been delayed for too long, and even if it passes in the future, it will not compensate for the reduction in cotton fields. There was no progress in Washington. The delivery notice for the March contract was released for ten contracts today. Ultimately, Wall Street sold, and the stock market weakened and declined slightly again. The spot price fell by 5 pounds, and futures fell by 6 to 19 pounds. The British cotton spot price rose by one point, and futures fell by 2-3 points. Indian cotton futures traders sold and bulls liquidated, while Japanese traders bought and short positions covered, with Pingor rising by 0.25 to 0.5 rupees, and both Omra and White Lorikeet rising and falling by 0.25 rupees. Flour Trade Quiet

Publishing World

A Little Response and Question 209

— Zeng Jianping

—After Reading "Life Bookstore's Reply to 'Critique of Life's National Bibliography' Notice"—

Last week, because I wrote an article criticizing "Life's National Bibliography," it caused Life Bookstore to publish a "Notice" to defend the book's editor. The defense content is divided into five points, and I now respond and raise additional questions as follows:

1. My previous article mentioned "claiming to surpass a certain catalog," because I saw it in the book's preface. Mr. Yu Zhenhuan, the preface writer, said: "This compilation contains about 20,000 kinds. The classification is clear, compared with ××… General Catalog, ××… Catalog, etc., it feels abundant and outstanding, and can be a guide for reading." The preface is like a signboard displayed in the editor's book, but the editor can say "it seems that I cannot be responsible for it," this attitude greatly loses the "style of a national scholar," and Zeng Jianping does not want to argue further.

2. Regarding the Xin Ken version of "Outline of Capital" and the Qingyun version of "Capital" being listed as two versions, since Pingxin-jun diligently blames the typesetters, we naturally cannot complain on behalf of the printing workers.

3. Regarding a small number of books in the bibliography having annotations, Pingxin-jun believes that "the purpose is also to facilitate readers to choose and purchase reading materials, and there is no prejudice at all." These words are not only a misinterpretation but also a lie. Because the editor clearly stated in the book's "Editorial Rules": "For world-famous works, a circle is added before the book title, and for books with problematic content, a ▲ symbol is added before the book title. However, the above classification method inevitably includes the editor's subjective opinions, and errors are difficult to avoid..." Since it says there are "subjective opinions" and "errors are difficult to guarantee," then it seems unnecessary to spend money to publish a "Notice" to argue forcefully that there is no "prejudice."

4. Pingxin-jun believes that "For reference materials (such as rural economic data, etc.), investigation reports (such as geological and mineral investigation reports, etc.), and tool books, no symbols are added in the bibliography." Now, let's put aside this "exception" and ask from within the "rule": Why are most or even all of the books in the Buddhism section and section A of the General Overview of Chinese Economy, etc., not marked with symbols by the editor? If it is because the content of these books cannot be accurately determined for their depth, then it can be said to be the editor's "ignorance." If these books should also be "exceptions," then it is the editor's misinterpretation and sophistry. "Ignorance?" Misinterpretation? What does the editor have to say?

5. Finally, the editor believed that my statement "the purpose of compiling this bibliography is to "promote their own books"..." does not require any debate. In fact, I have a very big reason for saying the above. Because in pages 142-3 of the bibliography, regarding books on Fascism, there are a total of 37 books included. Of these 37 books, only Dong Zhixue's "Fascism," published by Life Bookstore, is marked with a "middle level" symbol indicating who can read it. If it was not supposed to mark fascist books, if it was an "exception," why did "Life" specifically mark the books they published themselves? The purpose of marking is said to be to "facilitate readers' purchase of books," so it seems not too much to say that the editor is "promoting their own books." Why is the editor so petty and arguing forcefully?

The first principle of reviewing books is to seek the clarity of truth with an objective attitude. Even if the review is harsher, it is to promote truth and seek facts, and there is no preconceived notion. Pingxin-jun, in the bibliography he edited, not only did not complete his "study of compilation" with a fair attitude, but also based on his "subjective opinions," listed "International General History," "Markmin's Twelve Lectures," and "Recent Supplementary Education in Various Countries," among other three books, as "problematic" books. I don't know what problems these three books have? Even if the above three books really have "problems," how could there be only these three books in the "General Bibliography"? Some people believe that "the study of compilation does not require annotation, does not require expressing the editor's opinions." However, the editor must express them. Is this attitude "admirable" or "spoiling"? We really don't want to spend the space of the "Publishing World" to do this unnecessary debate. As for Pingxin-jun returning my criticism to "Zeng-jun," then I can only accept it. Anyway, right and wrong have their own comments from onlookers, why should we not show our generosity?

Review of "Life's National Bibliography" 210

— Qingshui

Book statistics are extremely important, but compiling statistics for the entire country's books is not an easy task. Mr. Liu Yimou said it well, "Poor scholars write, wealthy families publish, government documents, social groups compile, there are often printed items that are only given as gifts, not sold in bookstores or listed in newspapers. Those who know the matter seek them out everywhere; those who do not know have no way to purchase them." In such a heavy and difficult task, Mr. Pingxin had a grand vision, "using one person's strength to undertake the complex labor of compilation," and published this thick "National Bibliography." It cannot be said that this is a very pleasing thing. Mr. Yu Zhenhuan [illegible] again and again praised Mr. Xu Pingxin: "I deeply recognize the difficulty and admire his perseverance. From morning to evening, his eyes touch all the book titles, names of people, shops, institutions, prices, etc. His hands record all the book titles, names of people, shops, institutions, prices, etc. How boring is it? Collecting materials is also very difficult... The editor has seen many books handled, which is a hundred times better than those who see the titles but not the books." From this, it seems that this book should be very detailed and complete without any flaws. However, when we flip through it, we cannot help but be disappointed. Not only are the things we don't know difficult to find in the book, but also the things we know well are not found, which is strange. To enable the editor to make supplements in the next edition to achieve perfection, let me talk about one part of folklore studies. Other parts are limited by space and time, so I will not mention them for now.

Speaking of the beginning of Chinese folklore studies, we must respect the "Folksong Research Association" of Peking University, led by Shen Jianshi, Gu Jiegang, Liu Bannong, Chang Hui, Zhou Zuoren, Wei Jiangong, Bai Dizhou, Qian Xuantong, and others. They are all famous scholars who have worked hard and published "Folksong Weekly" (later compiled into a collection), "Guoxue Men Weekly," and printed special books (Mr. Dong Zuobin and Mr. Gu Jiegang both have collections of folksongs). Their achievements are not bad, and no one will forget them. Mr. Pingxin, the editor of this book, knows about folklore studies but does not know about the Folksong Research Association. Not only is the compilation of "Folksong Weekly" not included, but even special books such as "Wu Song" and "Seeing Her" cannot be found. Is this not a strange thing? "Life" does not have these books, they should also flip through the library's bibliography. No, such an unusual "missing one, leaving out ten thousand" is a great stain on this book.

Secondly, speaking of the books of the Folklore Society of Zhongda University in Guangzhou, my compilation "Daughter of the Sea Dragon King" (3 角), has prefaces by Mr. Zhao Jingshen and Mr. Rong Zhaozu, and is a collection of folk tales from one place—Wengyuan, Guangdong. The editor did not include it. I don't know what the reason is? My opinion is that the editor only looked at the bibliography and did not look at the content, thinking that the name sounded too beautiful and did not look like a story book, so he crossed it out with one stroke. From this point of view, the editor's own words, "Merely dividing according to a book title will cause many jokes," can be given back to him. Conversely, we are a little hesitant to believe his words, "Do not borrow or buy books that have not been read and flip through them."

Furthermore, the efforts and achievements of the China Folklore Society in Hangzhou are also not weak. The heads of similar academic institutions in Germany and Japan have also given considerable praise. The editor knows that they published "Folklore Compilation," but why doesn't he know about the books printed by them and their partners in the Shaoxing Tangpu Folk Publishing Department? (Not counting those printed individually)

(Collection of Legends)

The Sun and the Moon, Compiled by Qingshui, 2 角 5 分

The Story of Li Diaoyuan, Compiled by Ye Dejun, 1 角 5 分

Moonlight Folksong Collection, Compiled by Lou Yukuang, 1 角 5 分

Grandma Tiger Story Collection, Compiled by Zhong Jingwen, 1 角 5 分

Folklore Compilation, Lin Peilu, 3 角

New Year Customs Record, Lou Zikuang, 6 角

(Note) The editor says the publisher of this book is "Ta Kung Pao," which is incorrect. In January of the 24th year, it had been changed to be published by the Commercial Press, priced at 3 角 5 分. The editor also did not know this.

These are not private books, you can buy them, borrow them, and read them. The editor did not even know about them. It is very clear that he did not search widely and has many omissions. Other books published by several well-known partners of folk studies in various places, such as Lin Peiyu's "Chaozhou Folk Tales Collection" (Shantou Kaiming Bookstore), "Li Zichang Loves Painting," Xie Yunsheng's "Fujian Story Collection" (4 volumes, Xiamen China Bookstore), Weng Guoliang and Guosheng brothers' "Zhangzhou Folk Tales Collection," Wang Zhizhang's "Zhangzhou Folksongs," Cao Songye's "Jinhua Riddles," etc., dozens of volumes, were not searched and included. The publications of various local folk education halls have not yet been included. It is a pity. (I also have a story collection "Magician," published by Guangdong Weng Lianxing Bookstore, priced at 1 角 2 分 per volume.)

There are also some errors in book titles or author names; I have already said a lot, so I will not say more.

Overall, the publication of this bibliography in our current China is indeed unique and without any more details. It is also commendable that one person can do this. However, it is not the case that the national bibliography is limited to this number. I hope that Mr. Pingxin will not be satisfied with this and will continue to make improvements and supplements to seek perfection. It is best to inquire and ask the relevant institutions or scholars in each department and branch, and spend more postage and time, then the results obtained will be more satisfactory and reliable. By searching widely and supplementing as much as possible, and striving for perfection without being afraid of trouble, it will surely be more detailed and impressive than before after a year. The beginning of the compilation of a huge work is inevitably prone to errors or shallowness. Zheng Zhenduo's "Outline of Literature" is like this, and Feng Youlan's "Philosophy of Life" is like this. The Commercial Press's "Ciyuan" has been published for so long and still cannot fully satisfy people, let alone this first edition of the "National Bibliography"? However, from having mistakes to having no mistakes, from being crude and simple to being detailed and specialized, the editor should always keep this kind of mentality in mind and strive for it, so that good results can be expected. If not, harboring prejudices and considering others' fair comments as attacks, then it will end as crudely as it began, which is not what I want to say.

Bookstore Miscellany (Continued) 211

— Li Hengzhi

However, new literature had not yet established any foundation, and literary works manufactured in a crude manner were already flooding the market. Many were no more than articles from middle school composition notebooks, which, when printed, could also become fine collections of literature. For example, publications at the time, like "Tai Dong," only featured some wild shouts. As for "Zhen Mei Shan" (Truth, Beauty, Goodness), besides the translations of the Zeng father and son, there was nothing truly beautiful or good to be seen. Furthermore, those that were inferior to these need not be mentioned. In this way, so-called new literature was bound to be slowly rejected by people.

At the same time, after the raging tide of the National Revolution, everyone's understanding of the current society needed theoretical explanation, which could not be satisfied by simple literary appeals. Thus, the second trend that followed entered the period of social sciences. The introduction of emerging social sciences naturally had its objective needs, but this trend was ruined by the philistines in the new book industry from the very beginning. They published social science books indiscriminately, translating many famous works into incomprehensible gibberish, causing many young people to be intimidated by the emerging social sciences. For example, the United Bookstore, which is now merged into Modern, soon after its establishment, continued to publish literature books and children’s books. And they touted themselves as a "specialized social science bookstore." It can be imagined that social science books at that time were a source of profit for the philistines in the book industry. However, good times never last. This trend, due to the instigation of political parties and the speculation of philistines, finally disappeared shortly afterward. Many social science books could not be published, and some were not welcomed by readers. This period came to an end.

What followed was another wave of literary books, but it was different from the initial one. At this time, due to the cultivation of theory and the further demands of readers on the content of literary books, the so-called revolutionary literature movement occurred. Generally, new bookstores thought that the sales of literary books were still good after all, and they started a competition for literary books again. As a result, this movement declined again due to various reasons.

This period made the editors of new bookstores very bewildered. Literary books were no good, and social science books were no good either, so what kind of books should they publish? In their bewilderment, they heard that the Children's Bookstore was making money, and the children's books of the Commercial Press and China Bookstore were also selling well, so everyone turned to attack the children and primary school students. However, soon, the two major bookstores, the Commercial Press and the China Bookstore, launched large-scale sales such as the Children's Library and the Primary School Student's Library. The smaller bookstores could only succumb to the iron rule of large capital squeezing out small capital.

Children's books failed, so everyone thought, textbooks are something students have to buy, maybe there's a way. Come on, let's publish textbooks. You need to know that textbooks are fundamentally a mass-produced or monopolized business by large capital. How can small bookstores get involved? Middle school textbooks are all 20% off, primary school textbooks are all 40% off, the Commercial Press, China Bookstore, World Bookstore, and Datong Bookstore started the main battle. Those with weaker strength could only be defeated. Other small bookstores, learning from the nearby examples, naturally had to avoid this path.

Up to this point, due to the decline in the general purchasing power in the country, the new book industry has embarked on a stage of collapse. The last glimmer of hope was the simultaneous appearance of ancient books and magazines. Publishing ancient books meant that only libraries and collectors still had some purchasing power. Publishing magazines meant that the public's demand for knowledge was no longer specialized books, but short articles in magazines, and among magazines, especially humorous publications and picture magazines. — Recently, it has even moved from magazines to small newspapers, and new bookstores will slowly be excluded from the cultural circle. (According to my own observation, the development of small newspapers in China today, when education has not been popularized to the public, is only a sign of a further decline in culture, because small newspapers cannot create new readers, and their readers are still only those who read large newspapers and magazines.)

Look, what books have various bookstores published in the past year or two, whether in terms of quality or quantity? Today, the Commercial Press is the most diligent in publishing new books, publishing two or more every day. However, partly due to the objective conditions of China, it is not easy to produce scholars who are deeply researched, so there are also very few books of high value written. Looking at the new books of the Commercial Press every day, there are few new ideas of value and significance, and the general situation can be inferred. Other bookstores have mostly reduced the number of books published, let alone the quality of the books. Some bookstores are still publishing books, but the times seem to be reversing. The standard of publishing books is only regressing. Some, although not yet to the point of competing with philistines for profit by "20% off and 20% off," the publication of boring speculative books has occupied a major position. For example, "XX 100-Day Pass," "Practical XX Method," etc. are quite popular. Sometimes, because it is related to the reputation of their bookstore, they dare not publish it openly, so they fabricate the name of a bookstore. On the surface, there is only a consignment relationship, but in reality, it is all their own stuff. In terms of publishing books, the vigorous vitality of new bookstores is long gone. (To be continued)

Dr. Yao Juyan's Clinical Report on Gonorrhea 221

Clinic at the corner of Sichuan Road and Ningbo Road. Hours are 10:00 AM to 6:00 PM.

Unnoticeable Gonorrheal Urethritis

The mucous membrane and eye mucous membrane are the easiest places for gonococci to parasitize and grow. However, the eye mucous membrane is rarely infected, and the urethral membrane is the part that every gonorrhea patient must develop. If this part is not infected first, it will never be severe gonorrhea. However, once ordinary people contract this disease, it first affects the anterior urethra, which is anterior urethritis. If you do not immediately ask an experienced doctor to fundamentally solve it, the gonococci will get an inch and move to the posterior urethra, which is posterior urethritis. Posterior urethritis is more difficult to treat than anterior urethritis. However, many patients often ignore it and still do not deal with it. As a result, urethral stricture, orchitis, cystitis, etc. are all caused by urethritis that is not paid attention to. What is even more terrifying is that, according to my usual experience, many men who have been infertile for a long time are caused by the occurrence of posterior urethritis. This is because various changes and diseases caused by posterior urethritis often damage reproductive function.

There is a Mr. Qin Huoyu who lives on Fujian Road. According to his own description, he started to suffer from gonorrhea due to neglecting treatment. Later, his urethral opening became small, and he could hardly urinate. Recently, his testicles also felt swollen and painful, which is the beginning of orchitis. I used anti-gonorrheal serum and X-ray therapy, and at the same time gave him the internal medicine "Ke Lin Nong" (Gonorrhea Conqueror). He recovered after about three weeks.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talks

Talking About "Birth Control" Again 222

— Chui

Mrs. Sanger from the United States, who advocates "birth control," has recently arrived in Shanghai again. This is the second time she has come to China to promote her "birth control" doctrine.

The local press has had two factions, one in favor of and one against Mrs. Sanger's proposition. I was originally not very willing to talk about this issue. It is okay to be in favor, and it is also okay to be against, because being in favor is only theoretical, and I am afraid that it will not have any effect in practice, so in practice, there is no need to oppose it.

Now I will discuss it from a theoretical point of view. According to the most powerful argument against "birth control," it is said that "only the intellectual class in China can accept Mrs. Sanger's proposition. The intellectual class are excellent people. If the parents of intelligent children "control birth," only poor and ignorant farmers and workers will give birth to children. They have no ability to educate them and will eventually become stray children."

I have some objections to this proposition. First, I want to ask whether the children born to excellent people are necessarily excellent people. Whether or not they are excellent probably does not depend on race, but on education. Second, I want to ask whether excellent people are more likely to have the ability to live, or whether they are more likely to have money to cultivate their children. These two questions should be clarified first.

Speaking of the intellectuals of today, they are also very pitiful. Some starve to death, some commit suicide, some hold young children at home, some become thieves and robbers, some become traitors and treacherous merchants. Didn't a college student who had studied abroad rob a sea liner a few years ago? Didn't three college students in Zhejiang be shot a few years ago just because they became kidnappers? Are they intellectuals? Now, Yin Rugeng in North China and the many protagonists in the puppet shows outside the pass probably cannot be regarded as excellent people and intellectuals, right?

Let me turn around and ask, if excellent people are bound to give birth to excellent people, then the big pavilions will inevitably give birth to small Hengers, the big powerful people will inevitably give birth to small powerful people, and the big wealthy merchants will inevitably give birth to small wealthy merchants. But let me ask, of the so-called big bosses, the so-called powerful people, the so-called celebrities, and people who have productive capacity in society, and all people who can do things that benefit the masses in society, are their parents mostly excellent people? Although I cannot investigate them one by one, I am afraid that there are many whose parents are not excellent people but can strive out of difficulties and hardships, right?

In short, if the country is safe, the society is good, and it can develop rich resources and have productive industries, then adding one person will benefit one person. If the country is weak and various industries go bankrupt, adding one person will add one unemployed vagrant, one bandit, one traitor, and one criminal. Should we "control birth" or "not control birth"? Let me ask, what is the situation now?

Preacher 223

— Yonghui

Coming out of the bathhouse, I walked down the street with my head lowered. Suddenly, a hand patted my shoulder. Before I could even see his face, a white book was thrust into my chest. Without even waiting for me to examine the cover of the small book, he spoke:

"Have you been baptized?"

Looking down at the booklet in my hand, on which the words "Gospel" were neatly printed, I said:

"I have not been baptized."

"Then you should be baptized immediately." His gaze was certain, but his tone was almost commanding. "Where do you live? Is there a church there?"

"I live in Jing'an Temple."

"That's good. There's a church in Jing'an Temple. You should go every day." He opened the floodgates of his words, a string of phrases he had recited hundreds of times, gushing forth. "Do you know? Jesus is the Son of God. Everyone who believes in Jesus will be given eternal life by God and will ascend to heaven." Immediately, a look of intimidation and temptation appeared in his eyes: "You are a sinner. Not just you, everyone in the world is a sinner. You must know: those who do not believe in Jesus will go to hell." He pronounced the words "hell" with particular emphasis. "Do you understand what hell is? Ugh! Hell is where the Shanghainese 'devils' live!"

"Can believing in Jesus get me food to eat?" His sermon-like tone made me impatient.

"That's great. I'll go get baptized with you, but you have to treat me to a meal first." I made as if to leave with him.

"Hey! Don't just think about eating! Believe in God first, and of course you'll have food to eat. --- Look at me," he smoothed his hand over his chest, as if to straighten his clothes. "I came to Shanghai from my hometown without a single relative or a single copper, and I've survived for six or seven years. Ugh! As long as you believe in God, what's there to fear about having nothing to eat or wear?"

"When a person is very hungry, is there anything more important than eating?" I said indignantly.

"I'm telling you not to always think about eating..."

"What if I starve to death?" I interrupted.

"If you die, how can you believe in God?"

"I'm telling you, people who believe in God won't starve to death. Even if they die, they can go to heaven!" But immediately he corrected himself: "No, people who believe in God won't die, they will have eternal life! Not just us humans, God will protect even birds and insects. God is merciful!"

"Then why couldn't the birds in Tsuruga find food and thousands of them killed each other? Didn't they believe in God either?"

"That, that..." "That's impossible." His face turned red. "That, that God can't control so many things..." He was finally forced to confess by me, the inquisitor.

He was embarrassed and restless. Amidst the laughter of the onlookers, his sacred mask was shattered by me.

Two Women 224

— Huang Xu

She paced back and forth outside the madam's bedroom. She wrung her hands anxiously. One moment she would raise her hand to push open the door, the next she would shrink back in fear. She had repeated this hesitant action more than a dozen times.

Finally, she mustered her courage and pushed open the door, tiptoeing inside. Hearing the door open, the madam, who was playing mahjong, glanced at her. Pierced by that arrow-sharp gaze, the wide mouth with its two thick, clumsy lips immediately fell silent.

"Madam, Madam..." she stuttered, repeating the words twice, her face flushed and her thick lips trembling slightly.

"What is it?" the madam asked casually, with a touch of harshness, because her Clean Three Sides had just been won by the player on her left, and she was angry.

"Madam, I want, I want..." As usual, she repeated the words, just as she was about to slowly pour out the words she had prepared, when the madam suddenly turned half her face and snapped:

"What do you want?"

Startled, she forgot all the words she had prepared, and could only come straight to the point:

"I want... I want to borrow some money from you, Madam!..."

"Borrow money?" This time, the madam seemed surprised, and the other three female mahjong players also looked up. The madam turned her head and looked at the woman with disgust, saying, "What do you need the money for?"

"My man... is sick... very... sick... No money to hire... a doctor... buy medicine... I'm afraid... I'm afraid... for his life..." She said in a trembling voice, each word seeming to roll around, so it wasn't very clear. By the time she got to the last sentence, she dared not look up, and tears streamed down her face. She then used the corner of her clothes to wipe them away.

The madam hated and dreaded nothing more than someone borrowing money when she was gambling! Especially when the madam was having a bad hand, and especially when someone started crying in front of her near the end of the year! It was bad luck! At first, the madam had felt a little sorry for her, but later it turned to hatred, even animosity.

"Hmph, borrow money! You don't even know the rules. You're crying in front of me, bringing me bad luck!..." The more the madam thought about it, the angrier she became. She temporarily stopped playing mahjong, stood up, walked up to the woman, and said loudly:

"Get out of here! We don't need you here!"

It was like a bolt from the blue. The woman was stunned. With a thud, she instinctively knelt down.

"Madam, Madam, save me, save me!..." My man... my mother-in-law... my children all depend on me!..." Madam, Madam, I... I can't leave here!..."

She knelt on the floor, weeping and pleading, like a lamb in the hands of a wolf.

But it was no use! The madam still wore a fierce expression, showing no pity. Her proud self-esteem was threatening her! She felt that the more this woman did this, the more she insulted her dignity, and the more she made the three female mahjong players laugh at her! Infuriated, she raised her feet, wearing high-heeled leather shoes, and kicked the poor woman at random, shouting:

"Get out of here! Get out of here! We don't need you here!"

"Sister Li, don't get angry with this kind of person. Let's play mahjong!" The three female guests ran over, dragging and coaxing her to sit down.

The woman also stopped crying, got up, looked at the madam despairingly, and finally lifted her heavy steps, slowly, slowly walking out.

Now, the crisp sound of bamboo tiles rang out again in the madam's room.

Southern Journey Memories 225

— Yihua

In Tra Vinh

It was late autumn when I finally settled down in Tra Vinh.

For a wanderer, a prisoner of life, finding a job is an indescribably joyful experience. Even now, recalling the elation I felt when a Chinese merchant in Tra Vinh hired me as a tutor, I still feel a slight sense of comfort.

Tra Vinh is one of the six provinces of Annam, but in reality, it's just a larger market town in the countryside. If you look down from above, Tra Vinh must look like an isolated island surrounded by an ocean of emerald leaves. Living in such a market town, devoid of the clamor of city life, certainly has a unique flavor.

Our shop was by the river. In the morning, after telling the three children some stories, I would open the "Thousand Character Classic" to explain it to them and teach them to recite it. When we recited "Autumn ends, but the grass in Jiangnan does not wither," the children, growing up in a foreign land, naturally felt nothing, but I couldn't help but look out the window: outside, on the other side of the river, was a boundless ocean of green, and with the gusts of wind, the long wild grass stirred up gentle waves. Autumn was coming to an end, and the green grass in Jiangnan at that time might have been slightly yellow, but here it was still green, as green as early spring.

After lunch, everyone in the shop became drowsy. I moved a chair, sat down facing the river in the shade of the eaves, and stared blankly, as if lost, at the tall coconut groves, the blue sky, and the white clouds on the other side of the river.

"You are in a foreign land!" Looking at this scenery full of exotic charm, I whispered to myself. On the opposite bank, there were often Annamese people with dark complexions, bare chests, and red cloths wrapped around their waists, walking back and forth. They swayed as they walked, and the long, slightly curved sickles in their hands flashed. Seeing this scene often made me unconsciously imagine scenes from ancient times.

In Tra Vinh, nothing made me love it more than the stars. At night, the gentle breeze brought waves of unknown fragrance of grass. At that time, the stars in the deep blue sky were twinkling and whispering. They were so small, so dazzling, so small and dazzling like the tip of a needle, that people could not get used to them. Under the cover of the sky, I sat blankly in a trance. If you are a wandering person, you will know that in such scenery, what comes to my mind must be the thought of relatives and friends, and the longing for my hometown.

Opening "Fisherwoman's Morning Makeup"

The water in the pond is rising, and the fishing boats are moored. Willows hang down, covering ten thousand strands. At dawn, I only hear the orioles calling my dream. Quietly, the fisherwoman is busy throwing off the quilt lightly. She is, her body is thin and she lifts up. She is, her sleepy eyes are blurred and she is afraid to look closely. She is, she stretches lazily, yawning with her lotus arms. She is, she tidies up her clothes and bends her waist. But I see her, drawing water with a copper basin to wash her lotus face. But I see her, propping up the thatched window and supporting the bamboo pole. But I see her, picking up her clothes and adding half an arm. But I see her, lightly opening the mirror case and drawing her eyebrows. I also see her, tidying up a strand of spring cloud and combing it. Her hair is tied in the style of a nimble snake, charming. The powder box opens back, reflecting a startled wild goose. Furthermore, she carefully draws her eyebrows with willow charcoal. I can't describe her, her graceful appearance is charming. It will make people's souls melt at first sight. After finishing her makeup, the fisherwoman puts away her makeup tools. She calls out from the bow of the boat with a net in hand. Suddenly, I hear a light paddling of an oar.

Love Forum of Peach and Plum Competition 232

— Ye Ke

Li Pingqian's "Peach and Plum Competition", directed by Xiao Jiaozi, was originally renamed from "Love Letter". You Guangzhao's Secret to Love On the day that Yuan Lanjun (Moli) and Wang Zhengxin (Tiefu) got married, the best men were You Guangzhao, Wang Jiting, Sun Zheng, and Li Qing. On this day, in a corner of the reception room, You Dapangzi and a few others were holding a love forum. They talked about Lanjun and Zhengxin's marriage, and also talked about why the rigid Wang Zhengxin would marry Yuan Lanjun, a woman with such flexibility. Then, in their conversation, we can know that the fat You Guangzhao is the one who knows the secret to love best:

Sun: I really didn't expect that Tiefu (Wang Zhengxin) would marry this young lady (Yuan Lanjun), and they suddenly got engaged!

You: There's nothing surprising about that. The man has this (pointing to his head), has this (pointing to his strong body), and the woman has this (pointing to her face) and has this (gesturing for money)!

Sun: But wasn't he madly in love with Miss (Ye Qiuxin) before? How did it change again?

You: Because Miss has this (pointing to her face) but doesn't have this (gesturing for money)!

Wang Jiting's Love Experience, when they talked about this, Wang Jiting, the devil who specializes in playing with women, also joined in the discussion. His words may be very suitable for the expression of love among ordinary young people today:

Wang: It's not me being a pervert, but if it were me, I would want the second young lady, not the big young lady. Love is inherently stimulating. A woman who understands love is the one who can stimulate a man. Look at this second young lady, that kind of courage, that kind of means.

Chen Juanjuan has made great progress in Mandarin. Recently, a test screening of her dialogue portion in "Cimu Qu" (Song of a慈母 Loving Mother) revealed not only clear pronunciation but also excellent emotional expression in her language.

The shooting of Ma Long's (Jin Yan) bedroom in "Dao Ziran Qu" (To Nature) required a large number of items such as cow horns, clam shells, and large pumpkins. The production staff spent several days procuring these props before they could finally be prepared. Director Sun Yu said, "This film uses a lot of unusual props. In addition to those that need to be purchased at great expense, there are also many that need to be borrowed from the outside world. In short, the plot of this film is a bit special, so the things used are also a bit special."

Jin Yan's dog has already started appearing in shots in "Lang Tao Sha" (Sand of Waves). The dog has received long-term training and is very easy to work with in acting, helping the director. Zhang Zhizhi praised this dog as a divine dog of opportunity, capable of catching monkeys. If Zhuan Langen heard this, he would surely roll his eyes.

Chuan Jiqiu, the deputy head of the sound recording department, is very good at designing various sound effects and is also skilled in ventriloquism. He can imitate the sounds of a rooster crowing, a dog barking, a cat meowing, and a horse neighing, all of which are very realistic. He recently showcased his special skills in "Cimu Qu."

The grand Huacun scenery of "Mitu de Gaoyang" (The Lost Lamb), although having been rushed day and night for many days, has been completed, but due to continuous cloudy and rainy days recently, it has not been filmed. The schedule for shooting exterior scenes in Suzhou has also been postponed as a result. The crew is currently preparing for the main work, it is said.

"Yi Duo Hua" (A Flower) Short News 235

— Wenhua

"Yi Duo Hua" has officially started filming. Xu Manli plays the lead star of the song and dance troupe in the play, who is also a social butterfly.

The song and dance scenes in "Yi Duo Hua" will be guest-performed by a currently highly regarded song and dance troupe. However, the performance program will still employ experienced dance teachers with the latest and most beautiful artistic techniques from Europe and the United States to provide new training.

The songs in the song and dance scenes of "Yi Duo Hua" are being composed by Liu Xuechang, and it is said that they are quite rich in Eastern sentiment.

Yuan Meiyun plays an unsuccessful song and dance girl in "Yi Duo Hua," while Wang Yin plays the director of the song and dance troupe.

The plot of "Yi Duo Hua" is a sad, enchanting, lingering, and moving one.

The cinematographer of "Yi Duo Hua" is Wang Chunquan, the set designer is Bao Tianming, and the sound recorder is Gu Zongyi.

"Yi Duo Hua" is Xu Suling's first directorial work and is also one of the films that Yi Hua Company is working hard to produce this year.

Scattered Photography Notes on "Huashen Guniang" (Girl Incarnate) at Wing On 236

— Yulin

On the night of the fifteenth, "Huashen Guniang" filmed a scene in the department store of Wing On Company. More than one hundred employees of Yi Hua and about one hundred extras participated, as well as fifty or sixty people from Wing On. The liveliness was truly unprecedented.

Yuan Meiyun, wearing a handsome men's worker's suit, secretly walked around Nanjing Road alone. As a result, not only was she not surrounded, but no one could discover her secret.

The most difficult task that night was the configuration of the lighting, because the lighting frames were all temporarily installed. Moreover, when the light shone, the bright glass windows reflected light, so in addition to cinematographer Yao Shiquan, others such as Wang Chunquan, the cinematographer of "Yi Duo Hua," also helped with the configuration, taking great pains.

Director Fang Peilin was so busy that he didn't even have time to enjoy barbecued pork buns, and his throat was hoarse.

The most hardworking and meritorious should be the electricians and carpenters.

The colleagues at Wing On also provided great help in various aspects very enthusiastically, which simply made the Yi Hua authorities grateful.

Screenwriter Emil Gu Mu also stayed up all night, taking care of things in all aspects and sparing no effort.

Although Wang Guilin was ill, he still worked with illness and was full of energy, not showing any signs of pain.

Production clerk Chen Shu and stage manager Xi Liang, and set designer Da Ming ran around without stopping.

There was a long shot from the west corner to the east corner, which was the most difficult shot in the whole scene, but also the most exciting one.
